ہوتا ہے اور بھی عدد میں جیسے لوگ کہتے ہیں ہوالف رجل وہ ایک ہزار آدمیوں کے برابر ہے۔ یہاں قوت میں تشبیہ دینا مراد ہے۔ بہر حال اس کلام میں جب دو احتمال ہیں تو دونوں کی نیت کرنا درست ہے۔ اور اگر نیت نہ ہو تو ان دونوں میں جو اقل ہے وہ ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ اور ظاہر ہے کہ ایک بائنہ اقل ہے بمقابلہ تین طلاقوں کے اسوجہ سے ایک بائنہ واقع ہوگی۔ امام محمد سے روایت ہے کہ عدم نبیت کی صورت میں تین واقع ہوں گی کیونکہ الف عدد ہے۔ پس ظاہر یہ ہے کہ اس سے تشبیہ فی العدد مراد ہو۔ لہذا ایسا ہو گیا جیسا کسی نے کہا انت طالق کعد دالف اور اس صورت میں بالا تفاق تین واقع ہوں گی۔ لہذا کالف کہنے کی صورت میں بھی تین واقع ہونی چاہئیں ۔ اور تیسری مثال یعنی ایست طالق ملأ البیت اس سے طلاق بائن واقع ہونے کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ شی، کبھی گھر بھر دیتی ہے فی نفسہ عظیم اور بڑا ہونے کی وجہ سے۔ اور کبھی گھر بھر دیتی ہے کثرت کی وجہ سے۔ پس طلاق میں عظمت ظاہر ہوگی اہانت کے ذریعہ اور کثرت ظاہر ہو گی تین کے ذریعہ۔ لہذا ان دونوں احتمالات میں سے جس کی بھی نیت کرے گا درست ہوگی۔ اور عدم نیت کے وقت اقل ثابت ہو گا اور اقل ایک طلاق بائن ہے۔
Translation: And if a man says to his wife: 'You are divorced with the most severe divorce' or 'You are divorced like alif' or 'You are divorced filling the house', then one ba'in divorce occurs, unless he intends three. As for the first, because he has described divorce with severity, and severe divorce is ba'in because ba'in does not admit the possibility of being broken or abandoned; raj'i admits that possibility. And intention of three is valid because he mentioned the infinitive. As for the second, because sometimes tashbih in strength is intended, sometimes in number. It is said 'he is like a thousand men' meaning strength. So intending both matters is valid, and when intention is absent, the lesser of the two is established. It is narrated from Imam Muhammad that without intention three occur because alif is a number, so apparently tashbih in number is intended. So it becomes like one who says 'You are divorced like the number alif'. As for the third, because something sometimes fills the house due to its greatness and sometimes due to its multiplicity. So whoever intends any, his intention is valid, and when intention is absent the lesser is established. Then the rule according to Abu Hanifa: when divorce is compared to something, a ba'in divorce occurs, whatever the object of comparison, whether the word 'azm is mentioned or not. According to Abu Yusuf, if 'azm is mentioned then ba'in, otherwise not, whatever the object. According to Zufar, if the object of comparison is something that can be described as great in people's view, then ba'in occurs, otherwise raj'i. It is said that Muhammad is with Abu Hanifa, and it is said with Abu Yusuf. The manifestation of this difference is in his statement 'like the head of a needle' etc., i.e., like the head of a needle, like the bone of the head of a needle, like a mountain, like the bone of a mountain. Explanation: In this passage three examples of tashbih are mentioned. The ruling for all three is that a ba'in divorce occurs, and if three are intended they occur. The proof for the first: 'anti taliq ashadd al-talaq' describes divorce with severity, and severity is attained through baynunah because after baynunah divorce does not admit possibility of breaking. So we said this word makes a ba'in divorce; however if three are intended they occur because he mentioned the infinitive. The second example: 'anti taliq ka-alif'. Ba'in occurs because sometimes tashbih in strength is intended, sometimes in number. When there are two probabilities, intending both is correct, and if no intention the lesser is established. Imam Muhammad narrates that without intention three occur because alif is a number. The third example: 'anti taliq mal' al-bayt'. Ba'in occurs because something fills the house due to greatness or multiplicity. So in talaq, greatness appears through one talaq and multiplicity through three. So whichever he intends is correct, and without intention the lesser is one ba'in.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on three specific divorce phrases that imply exaggeration. The commentary explains that each phrase results in a single ba'in divorce unless the husband intended three. The reasoning is that the words 'ashadd' (most severe) and 'ka-alif' (like alif, meaning a thousand or strength) and 'mal' al-bayt' (filling the house) all add a quality of intensity or completeness that makes the divorce ba'in. The passage also introduces an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Muhammad holds that 'ka-alif' without intention yields three divorces because 'alif' is a clear number. The text then presents a general rule (qāʻidah) for tashbih: according to Abu Hanifa, any tashbih makes the divorce ba'in; according to Abu Yusuf, only if the word 'azm (greatness) is mentioned; according to Zufar, only if the object compared is inherently great in people's estimation. The passage concludes by applying this rule to the examples, showing where the imams agree and disagree.

Key Terms
بائن (bā'in): A type of talaq where the marriage is irrevocably dissolved; the husband cannot take back his wife without a new marriage contract.
رجعی (raj'ī): A revocable divorce where the husband may take back his wife during the waiting period without a new contract.
تشبیہ (tashbīh): Comparing the divorce to something else, which adds a qualitative meaning indicating intensity or greatness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband says to his wife 'anti taliq ka-alif' without any intention, what is the ruling according to the majority Hanafi position?
A) One raj'i divorce occurs.
B) Three divorces occur.
C) One ba'in divorce occurs.
D) No divorce occurs.

Key Takeaway
Exaggerated divorce phrases result in one ba'in divorce by default; intention of three must be explicit, and ambiguity is resolved by taking the minimum.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
12 min
Described Talaq and the Effect of Tashbih: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
States the principle for adjectives in talaq and applies it to tashbih with four examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle on described talaq to classify a tashbih expression and state whether the resulting talaq is raj'i or ba'in according to each of the four imams.

Core Idea
A divorce compared to something becomes ba'in only when it adds greatness—but the imams differ on what counts as greatness.

This lesson delves into a nuanced area of Hanafi talaq law: when a husband uses a descriptive adjective or a comparison (tashbih) in pronouncing divorce. The source passage from al-Hidayah establishes a general rule for descriptions that are irrelevant or do not add meaning, and then presents the famous dispute over tashbih. We will walk through the principle and the four positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Zufar, and Muhammad, and see how they apply to four concrete examples.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish between descriptions that apply to divorce and those that do not
First, determine if the attribute (e.g., 'like the head of a needle') is one that can actually describe a divorce. If not, it is lughw and the talaq remains raj'i.
Example: 'A divorce that does not affect you' is lughw.
2
Check if the description adds a new quality
If the description applies to divorce (like 'most beautiful'), see if it merely elaborates or adds a benefit. If it adds no new meaning, talaq is raj'i; if it adds something, we move to tashbih analysis.
Example: 'most complete divorce' adds no new quality, so raj'i.
3
Identify tashbih and its components
For tashbih (comparison), note the mushabbah bihi (object of comparison) and whether the word 'azm (greatness/bone) is explicitly mentioned.
Phrases like 'like a mountain' are tashbih.
4
Apply each imam's rule
Abu Hanifa: any tashbih makes it ba'in. Abu Yusuf: only if 'azm is mentioned. Zufar: only if the object is commonly considered great. Muhammad's position is unsettled.
For 'like the head of a needle', Abu Hanifa says ba'in, others raj'i.
5
Derive the ruling for each example and note the practical consequence
Use the four examples to see how the difference plays out: small objects, objects with 'azm, large objects, etc. The thamarah al-khilaf is the type of talaq (raj'i vs. ba'in).
The only unanimous ba'in case is 'like the bone of a mountain'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الاصل سے صاحب ہدایہ نے ایک ضابطہ بیان فرمایا ہے جس پر ائمہ ثلثہ اور امام زفر کے اقوال منی ہیں ۔ ضابطہ یہ ہے کہ اگر طالق کو ایسے وصف کے ساتھ موصوف کیا گیا جس کے ساتھ طلاق کو موصوف نہیں کیا جاتا۔ تو یہ وصف لغو ہوگا ۔ اور طلاق رجعی واقع ہوگی۔ مثلاً کہا انت طالق طلاقاً لا يقع علیک اور اگر ایسا وصف ہے جس کے ساتھ طلاق کو متصف کیا جاتا ہے تو اس کی دو صورتیں ہیں۔ مفید زیادت ہے یا نہیں۔ اگر زیادتی کا فائدہ نہیں دیتا تو اس صورت میں بھی طلاق رجعی واقع ہوگی ۔ مثلاً کہا انست طالق احسن الطلاق يا اجمل الطلاق يا اكمل الطلاق یا افضل الطلاق ۔ اور اگر مفید زیادت ہے تو حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ فرماتے ہیں کہ طلاق کو جب کسی چیز کے ساتھ تشبیہ دی جائے تو طلاق بائن واقع ہوگی مشبہ بہ کچھ بھی ہو۔ لفظ عظم تشبیہ میں مذکور وہ یا مذکور نہ ہو۔ دلیل سابق میں گذر چکی کہ مطلقاً تشبیہ زیادتی وصف کا تقاضا کرتی ہے۔ اور امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر لفظ اعظم تشبیہ میں مذکور ہے تو طلاق بائن واقع ہوگی ورنہ نہیں ۔ مشبہ بہ کچھ بھی ہو ۔ اسلئے کہ تشبیہ کبھی عظمت کے معنی خالی کر کے صرف ایک ہونے میں ہوتی ہے۔ اور لفظ عظم کا ذکر تو یقینا زیادتی کے معنی پیدا کرے گا۔ اور امام زفر فر ماتے ہیں کہ اگر مشبہ بہ ایسی چیز ہے جو لوگوں کے نزدیک عظیم شمار ہوتی ہے تو اس صورت میں طلاق بائن واقع ہو گی ۔ ورنہ رجعی ہوگی لفظ عظم مذکور ہو یا نہ ہو، امام محمد کا قول مضطرب ہے۔ ابوحنیفہ کے ساتھ بھی ہو سکتا ہے اور ابو یوسف ہو کے ساتھ بھی۔ اس اختلاف کا ثمرہ مندرجہ ذیل مثالوں میں ظاہر ہوگا ، انت طالق مثل راس الأبرة اس مثال میں امام صاحب کے نزدیک بائن ہوگی اور امام ابو یوسف اور امام زفر کے نزدیک رجعی ہوگی ۔ اور انت طالق مثل عظم راس الابرة میں امام صاحب اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک بائن ہوگی۔ اور امام زفر کے نزدیک رجعی اور است طالق مثل الجبل میں امام صاحب اور امام زفر کے نزدیک بائن ہوگی ۔ اور ابو یوسف کے نزد یک رجعی اور انت طالق مثل عظم الجبل میں تینوں کے نزدیک بائن ہوگی۔ امام صاحب کے نزدیک تشبیہ کی وجہ سے اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک لفظ عظیم مذکور ہونے کی وجہ سے اور امام زفر کے نزدیک اسلئے کہ جبل عام لوگوں کے نزدیک عظیم ہے۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب
Then the author of Hidayah stated a principle from the asl, upon which the three imams and Imam Zufar's statements are based. The principle is: If the divorced woman is described with a description that does not apply to divorce, then that description is ignored (lughw) and the divorce is raj'i. For example, 'You are divorced with a divorce that does not affect you.' And if it is a description that does apply to divorce, then there are two situations: either it adds a benefit or not. If it does not add benefit, then also raj'i, e.g., 'You are divorced with the best divorce' or 'most beautiful divorce' or 'most complete divorce' or 'most excellent divorce'. And if it does add benefit, then Imam Abu Hanifa says: When divorce is compared to something, a ba'in divorce occurs, whatever the object of comparison, whether the word 'azm is mentioned or not. The proof has passed that tashbih absolutely requires the addition of a quality. Imam Abu Yusuf says: If the word 'azm is mentioned in the tashbih, then ba'in; otherwise not, whatever the object, because tashbih sometimes occurs without meaning of greatness, just in essence. And mentioning 'azm certainly creates the meaning of addition. Imam Zufar says: If the object of comparison is something that is considered great among people, then ba'in occurs; otherwise raj'i, whether the word 'azm is mentioned or not. Imam Muhammad's statement is unsettled; it could be with Abu Hanifa or with Abu Yusuf. The fruit of this difference appears in the following examples: 'You are divorced like the head of a needle': according to Imam Abu Hanifa ba'in, according to Abu Yusuf and Zufar raj'i. 'You are divorced like the bone of the head of a needle': according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf ba'in, according to Zufar raj'i. 'You are divorced like a mountain': according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Zufar ba'in, according to Abu Yusuf raj'i. 'You are divorced like the bone of a mountain': according to all three ba'in - for Abu Hanifa due to tashbih, for Abu Yusuf due to mentioning 'azm, for Zufar because a mountain is considered great among common people. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage establishes a general principle (asl) regarding descriptions in talaq. The principle categorizes descriptions into three types: (1) those that do not apply to divorce at all (lughw, resulting in raj'i talaq), (2) those that apply but do not add new meaning (resulting in raj'i talaq), and (3) those that apply and add a quality of excess. Within the third type, the dispute among the Hanafi imams is detailed: Abu Hanifa rules that any tashbih (comparison) makes the talaq ba'in because it inherently adds quality; Abu Yusuf requires the explicit word 'azm (greatness) for it to be ba'in; Zufar considers the common perception of the object's greatness. The passage then applies this dispute to four concrete examples: 'like the head of a needle' (small object), 'like the bone of the head of a needle' (emphasizing smallness), 'like a mountain' (large object), and 'like the bone of a mountain' (emphasizing largeness). The examples show how each imam's rule yields different results, with only the last example being unanimously ba'in.

Key Terms
عظم (ʿaẓm): Literally 'bone' but in this context refers to 'greatness' or 'magnitude' as a descriptive element in comparisons.
لغو (laghw): An irrelevant or meaningless description that does not apply to divorce and thus has no legal effect.
مشبہ بہ (mushabbah bihī): The object to which the divorce is compared in a tashbih expression.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 'You are divorced like the head of a needle'
B) 'You are divorced like the bone of the head of a needle'
C) 'You are divorced like a mountain'
D) 'You are divorced like the bone of a mountain'

Key Takeaway
The effect of tashbih in talaq depends on whether the comparison adds greatness; the imams differ on the condition, but the majority (Abu Hanifa and Zufar for great objects) find it ba'in.

Ruling for Talaq Described as Severe, Broad, or Long
States the ruling for talaq described as severe, broad, or long

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a husband describes talaq as shadidah, areedah, or taweelah, and distinguish the majority Hanafi view from Abu Yusuf's position.

Core Idea
Adjectives describing the divorce as severe, broad, or long make it a single ba'in divorce unless three are intended.

This passage addresses a specific expression in divorce: when the husband uses adjectives to characterize the divorce itself. The Hanafi majority holds that such language implies finality, making the divorce irrevocable (ba'in). However, Abu Yusuf argues these adjectives are not legally meaningful and should be ignored, leaving the divorce as raj'i. Understanding this difference is crucial for determining the woman's status and the possibility of reconciliation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the expression
Recognize the phrase: 'You are divorced with a severe divorce' (and similar). The adjectives are attached to the divorce (tatliqatan), not the woman.
These adjectives are metaphorical.
2
State the default ruling
According to the majority (Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf's later view? Actually Abu Yusuf differs, but the text says the majority is ba'in). The ruling is one ba'in divorce.
Ba'in means the husband cannot take her back without a new marriage.
3
Understand the reasoning
The adjectives indicate irreparability and finality, which are characteristics of ba'in divorce. The text uses the logic: 'that which cannot be repaired is severe, and ba'in is of that nature.'
This is a talil (reasoning by attribute).
4
Note the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf holds that these adjectives are not legally appropriate for divorce, so they are ignored, resulting in a raj'i divorce.
Raj'i allows the husband to take her back during iddah without a new contract.
5
Apply the intention rule
If the husband intends three divorces, his intention is valid because 'severity' can be understood as threefold, and three ba'in divorces occur.
This is consistent with the general Hanafi principle that intention affects the number when the expression is not explicit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
انت طالق تطليقة شديدة او عريضة او طويلة فهى واحدة بائنة لان مالايمكن تداركه يشتد عليه وهو البائن وما يصعب تداركه يقال لهذا الامرطول وعرض وعن ابى يوسف انه يقع بهارجعية لان هذا الوصف لايليق به فيلغوولو نوى الثلث في هذه الفصول صحت نيته لتنوع البينونة على مامرو الواقع بهابائن
And if he says 'You are divorced with a severe, or broad, or long divorce', then it is one ba'in, because that which cannot be repaired is severe and it is ba'in, and that which is difficult to repair is called long and broad. And from Abu Yusuf that it occurs as raj'i because this description is not befitting to divorce, so it is ignored. And if he intends three in these instances, his intention is valid due to the variety of baynunah, as has passed, and what occurs is ba'in.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling for describing the divorce itself (not the woman) with adjectives like shadidah (severe), areedah (broad), or taweelah (long). The majority holds that such descriptions make the divorce ba'in because they imply a finality that is characteristic of irrevocable divorce. Abu Yusuf disagrees, arguing that these adjectives do not legitimately apply to divorce and are therefore ignored, leaving the divorce as raj'i. The passage also notes that if the husband intends three with these words, his intention is valid because the concept of 'severity' can be understood as threefold, and three ba'in divorces would occur.

Key Terms
شديدة (shadīdah): Severe, indicating an irreversible or extreme form of divorce.
عريضة (ʿarīḍah): Broad or wide, metaphorically indicating difficulty of reconciliation.
طويلة (ṭawīlah): Long, metaphorically indicating a lengthy or irretrievable separation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) No divorce occurs.

Key Takeaway
Describing talaq as shadidah, areedah, or taweelah results in one ba'in divorce unless three are intended, and Abu Yusuf's contrary view is not the relied-upon position.

Two Probabilities in Talaq: The Lesser Applies
Ruling on ambiguous talaq expressions with two probabilities

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle that when a talaq expression admits two probabilities, the husband's intention governs, and in its absence the lesser number applies, using the examples of 'kalf' and 'mala'a al-bayt'.

Core Idea
When talaq wording is ambiguous, intention decides; without intention, the lesser number applies.

In the Hanafi school, the validity of a talaq often depends on the husband's explicit or implicit intention. This lesson examines expressions that can bear two meanings, such as 'kalf' (like the letter alif or a mount) and 'mala'a al-bayt' (fill the house). The ruling establishes that the husband may intend either meaning, and if he has no intention, the lesser number of talaqs falls — one ba'in rather than three. We also explore Imam Muhammad's dissenting view on 'kalf'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ambiguous expression
Determine which part of the talaq pronouncement carries two possible meanings. For example, 'kalf' can mean 'like the letter alif' (a number) or 'like a mount' (tall).
2
Determine the two probabilities
List the two possible numbers/effects and their rationales. For 'kalf', the two probabilities are one ba'in (if likened to a mount) or three talaqs (if likened to the letter alif as a numerical symbol).
3
Apply the default rule
If the husband had an intention, follow it. If not, apply the lesser number (one ba'in) according to the majority (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf).
The principle: ma' al-ittifaq 'adam al-niyyah, al-aqall yuthbat.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Recognize that Imam Muhammad argues for three in 'kalf' due to the numerical connotation of 'alif', and understand why the majority rejects this. The majority considers the analogy to 'ka'addad alif' imperfect because 'kalf' is a generic comparison.
This ikhtilaf is legitimate; the mufta bihi is the majority view.

کتاب الطلاق میں جب دو احتمال ہیں تو دونوں کی نیت کرنا درست ہے۔ اور اگر نیت نہ ہو تو ان دونوں میں جو اقل ہے وہ ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ اور ظاہر ہے کہ ایک بائنہ اقل ہے بمقابلہ تین طلاقوں کے اسوجہ سے ایک بائنہ واقع ہوگی۔ امام محمد سے روایت ہے کہ عدم نبیت کی صورت میں تین واقع ہوں گی کیونکہ الف عدد ہے۔ پس ظاہر یہ ہے کہ اس سے تشبیہ فی العدد مراد ہو۔ لہذا ایسا ہو گیا جیسا کسی نے کہا انت طالق کعد دالف اور اس صورت میں بالا تفاق تین واقع ہوں گی۔ لہذا کالف کہنے کی صورت میں بھی تین واقع ہونی چاہئیں ۔ اور تیسری مثال یعنی ایست طالق ملأ البیت اس سے طلاق بائن واقع ہونے کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ شی، کبھی گھر بھر دیتی ہے فی نفسہ عظیم اور بڑا ہونے کی وجہ سے۔ اور کبھی گھر بھر دیتی ہے کثرت کی وجہ سے۔ پس طلاق میں عظمت ظاہر ہوگی اہانت کے ذریعہ اور کثرت ظاہر ہو گی تین کے ذریعہ۔ لہذا ان دونوں احتمالات میں سے جس کی بھی نیت کرے گا درست ہوگی۔ اور عدم نیت کے وقت اقل ثابت ہو گا اور اقل ایک طلاق بائن ہے۔
In the book of divorce: when there are two probabilities, it is correct to intend either. And if there is no intention, then the lesser of the two will be established. And it is obvious that one ba'in talaq is lesser compared to three talaqs; therefore one ba'in talaq will occur. It is narrated from Imam Muhammad that in case of no intention, three will occur because the letter 'alif' is a number. So it is apparent that by it resemblance in number is intended. Hence it becomes like someone saying 'anti taliq ka'addad alif' and in that case, by consensus, three will occur. Therefore, in the case of saying 'kalif', three should also occur. And the third example: 'anti taliq mala'a al-bayt' – the reason for one ba'in talaq occurring is that something sometimes fills the house due to greatness and enormity, and sometimes fills the house due to abundance. So in divorce, greatness appears through insult and abundance appears through three. Hence whichever of these two probabilities he intends will be correct. And at the time of no intention, the lesser is established, and the lesser is one ba'in talaq.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hidayah on talaq wording with two possible meanings. The author explains that when a husband uses a phrase that can be interpreted in two ways (e.g., 'kalf' meaning like the letter alif or like a mount), his intention determines the outcome. If he intends three, three occur; if he intends one ba'in, that occurs. If he has no intention, the lesser (one ba'in) applies by default. Imam Muhammad disagrees in the case of 'kalf', arguing that since 'alif' is a number, the phrase inherently indicates three, so even without intention three should fall. The passage also covers the phrase 'mala'a al-bayt' (fill the house), which can imply greatness (one ba'in) or abundance (three). The same principle applies: intention decides, else the lesser. This is a detailed expansion of the matn's ruling on ambiguous talaq expressions.

Key Terms
اقل (aqall): The lesser of two possible numbers of talaq (here one ba'in compared to three)
تشبیہ فی العدد (tashbih fi al-‘adad): Resemblance in number, i.e., the phrase 'kalf' is interpreted as comparing to the letter alif which is number one in counting, so it indicates one talaq.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband says 'anti taliq kalf' without any intention, how many talaqs fall according to the majority of Hanafi imams?
A) Three talaqs
B) One ba'in talaq
C) One raj'i talaq
D) No talaq

Key Takeaway
In ambiguous talaq expressions, the husband's intention decides; without intention, the lesser number (one ba'in) applies.

Talaq — Divorce

Talaq by Similitude: Ikhtilaf of the Three Imams
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on talaq by similitude

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Imam Zufar on talaq by similitude and apply their rulings to given phrases.

Core Idea
In talaq by similitude, Abu Hanifa always rules ba'in; Abu Yusuf requires the word 'greatness'; Zufar requires the object to be commonly considered great.

When a husband says things like 'you are divorced like a mountain' or 'like the tip of a needle', the ruling varies among Hanafi imams. This passage from al-Hidayah lays out a general rule about attributes in talaq and then details the ikhtilaf of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Zufar on when a similitude (tashbih) makes the talaq ba'in rather than raj'i. Understanding this ikhtilaf is essential for issuing accurate fatwas in such cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule on attributes
The author first states: if talaq is qualified with an attribute that does not befit talaq (laghw), the talaq remains raj'i. If the attribute does befit talaq, check whether it adds extra meaning (mufid ziyadah). If not, talaq is still raj'i.
Example of laghw: 'talaq that does not fall on you' — ignored. Example of non-beneficial attribute: 'ahsan al-talaq' — no extra meaning, raj'i.
2
Recognize the ikhtilaf on tashbih
When the attribute is a similitude (tashbih) that adds meaning (e.g., 'like a mountain'), the imams differ on when it becomes ba'in. Understand each position: Abu Hanifa: any similitude => ba'in. Abu Yusuf: only if word 'greatness' (عظم) is mentioned. Zufar: only if the object of comparison is commonly considered great.
The underlying principle: similitude implies an increase of attribute. The imams disagree on the necessary condition for that increase to be effective.
3
Apply the criteria to sample phrases
Work through the four examples given: (1) 'like a needle's head' (without greatness), (2) 'like the greatness of a needle's head', (3) 'like the mountain' (without greatness), (4) 'like the greatness of the mountain'.
For each, determine whether each imam would rule ba'in or raj'i.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: in some cases the talaq is ba'in, meaning the wife is immediately separated and can only return by a new marriage; in other cases it is raj'i, allowing reconciliation during the iddah.
For example, 'like a needle's head' is raj'i for Abu Yusuf and Zufar but ba'in for Abu Hanifa.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa, as it is precautionary and consistent with the principle that similitude implies increase.
Thus, for fatwa, any tashbih in talaq results in ba'in.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الاصل سے صاحب ہدایہ نے ایک ضابطہ بیان فرمایا ہے جس پر ائمہ ثلثہ اور امام زفر کے اقوال منی ہیں ۔ ضابطہ یہ ہے کہ اگر طالق کو ایسے وصف کے ساتھ موصوف کیا گیا جس کے ساتھ طلاق کو موصوف نہیں کیا جاتا۔ تو یہ وصف لغو ہوگا ۔ اور طلاق رجعی واقع ہوگی۔ مثلاً کہا انت طالق طلاقاً لا يقع علیک اور اگر ایسا وصف ہے جس کے ساتھ طلاق کو متصف کیا جاتا ہے تو اس کی دو صورتیں ہیں۔ مفید زیادت ہے یا نہیں۔ اگر زیادتی کا فائدہ نہیں دیتا تو اس صورت میں بھی طلاق رجعی واقع ہوگی ۔ مثلاً کہا انست طالق احسن الطلاق يا اجمل الطلاق يا اكمل الطلاق یا افضل الطلاق ۔ اور اگر مفید زیادت ہے تو حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ فرماتے ہیں کہ طلاق کو جب کسی چیز کے ساتھ تشبیہ دی جائے تو طلاق بائن واقع ہوگی مشبہ بہ کچھ بھی ہو۔ لفظ عظم تشبیہ میں مذکور وہ یا مذکور نہ ہو۔ دلیل سابق میں گذر چکی کہ مطلقاً تشبیہ زیادتی وصف کا تقاضا کرتی ہے۔ اور امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر لفظ اعظم تشبیہ میں مذکور ہے تو طلاق بائن واقع ہوگی ورنہ نہیں ۔ مشبہ بہ کچھ بھی ہو ۔ اسلئے کہ تشبیہ کبھی عظمت کے معنی خالی کر کے صرف ایک ہونے میں ہوتی ہے۔ اور لفظ عظم کا ذکر تو یقینا زیادتی کے معنی پیدا کرے گا۔ اور امام زفر فر ماتے ہیں کہ اگر مشبہ بہ ایسی چیز ہے جو لوگوں کے نزدیک عظیم شمار ہوتی ہے تو اس صورت میں طلاق بائن واقع ہو گی ۔ ورنہ رجعی ہوگی لفظ عظم مذکور ہو یا نہ ہو، امام محمد کا قول مضطرب ہے۔ ابوحنیفہ کے ساتھ بھی ہو سکتا ہے اور ابو یوسف ہو کے ساتھ بھی۔ اس اختلاف کا ثمرہ مندرجہ ذیل مثالوں میں ظاہر ہوگا ، انت طالق مثل راس الأبرة اس مثال میں امام صاحب کے نزدیک بائن ہوگی اور امام ابو یوسف اور امام زفر کے نزدیک رجعی ہوگی ۔ اور انت طالق مثل عظم راس الابرة میں امام صاحب اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک بائن ہوگی۔ اور امام زفر کے نزدیک رجعی اور است طالق مثل الجبل میں امام صاحب اور امام زفر کے نزدیک بائن ہوگی ۔ اور ابو یوسف کے نزد یک رجعی اور انت طالق مثل عظم الجبل میں تینوں کے نزدیک بائن ہوگی۔ امام صاحب کے نزدیک تشبیہ کی وجہ سے اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک لفظ عظیم مذکور ہونے کی وجہ سے اور امام زفر کے نزدیک اسلئے کہ جبل عام لوگوں کے نزدیک عظیم ہے۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب
Then from the principle, the author of Hidayah stated a rule upon which the three imams and Imam Zufar's statements are built. The rule is that if talaq is qualified with an attribute with which talaq is not qualified, then this attribute is لغو, and raj'i talaq will occur. For example, if he says 'anti taliq talaqan la yaqa'u 'alayki'. And if it is an attribute with which talaq can be qualified, then there are two cases: it is beneficial for increase or not. If it does not give the benefit of increase, then also raj'i talaq occurs. For example, if he says 'anti taliq ahsan al-talaq' or 'ajmal al-talaq' or 'akmal al-talaq' or 'afdal al-talaq'. And if it is beneficial for increase, then Imam Abu Hanifa says: when talaq is likened to something, then ba'in talaq occurs, no matter what the thing is compared to, whether the word 'greatness' is mentioned in the similitude or not. The proof has passed earlier that a similitude absolutely requires an increase of attribute. And Imam Abu Yusuf says: if the word 'greatness' is mentioned in the similitude, then ba'in talaq occurs, otherwise not, no matter what the thing is compared to. Because a similitude sometimes is stripped of the meaning of greatness and is just about being one. And mentioning the word 'greatness' certainly produces the meaning of increase. And Imam Zufar says: if the thing compared to is considered great among people, then ba'in talaq occurs, otherwise raj'i, whether the word 'greatness' is mentioned or not. Imam Muhammad's saying is inconsistent: it can be with Abu Hanifa and also with Abu Yusuf. The fruit of this difference will appear in the following examples: 'anti taliq mithl ras al-ibrah' – in this example, according to Imam Abu Hanifa it will be ba'in, and according to Abu Yusuf and Imam Zufar it will be raj'i. And 'anti taliq mithl 'azm ras al-ibrah' – according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf it will be ba'in, and according to Imam Zufar raj'i. And 'anti taliq mithl al-jabal' – according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Zufar it will be ba'in, and according to Abu Yusuf raj'i. And 'anti taliq mithl 'azm al-jabal' – according to all three it will be ba'in: according to Imam Abu Hanifa because of similitude, according to Abu Yusuf because the word 'great' is mentioned, and according to Imam Zufar because the mountain is considered great among common people. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage sets out a key principle from the Hidayah regarding talaq qualified by attributes. The principle: if the attribute does not befit talaq (e.g., 'talaq that does not fall on you'), it is disregarded and raj'i talaq occurs. If the attribute does befit talaq, we check if it adds extra meaning. If no extra meaning (like 'best talaq'), it also results in raj'i. If it adds extra meaning, there is ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa holds that any talaq by similitude (tashbih) is ba'in, regardless of whether 'greatness' is mentioned, because a similitude inherently implies an increased attribute. Abu Yusuf requires the word 'greatness' to be explicitly mentioned for ba'in; otherwise, the similitude may be merely quantitative (one). Imam Zufar looks at whether the object of comparison is commonly considered great by people, regardless of the word 'greatness'. The passage gives concrete examples: a needle's head is not great, so only Abu Hanifa calls it ba'in; a mountain is great, so Abu Hanifa and Zufar call it ba'in even without 'greatness'. With 'greatness' explicitly mentioned, Abu Yusuf also joins. This illustrates the practical application of their usul.

Key Terms
تشبیہ (tashbih): A statement likening talaq to something else, e.g., 'anti taliq mithl al-jabal'
لغو (laghw): Void/meaningless – an attribute that does not apply to talaq is ignored and the talaq remains raj'i
مفید زیادت (mufid ziyadah): An attribute that adds extra meaning (e.g., 'severe' as opposed to 'beautiful')

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab's mufta bihi, what is the ruling if a husband says 'anti taliq mithl ras al-ibrah' (like the tip of a needle) without mentioning greatness?
A) Talaq raj'i
B) Talaq ba'in
C) No talaq
D) Talaq is suspended

Key Takeaway
In talaq by similitude, the Hanafi madhhab relies on Abu Hanifa's position that any tashbih yields ba'in, while Abu Yusuf and Zufar have more restrictive criteria.

Talaq with Descriptors of Severity: Shadida, Arida, Tawila
Ruling on talaq with descriptors of severity and its proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on talaq qualified by 'shadida' (severe), 'arida' (wide), or 'tawila' (long), and distinguish between the majority view (ba'in) and Abu Yusuf's position (raj'i).

Core Idea
Talaq described as 'severe' or 'wide' indicates irreparability, hence it is ba'in, not raj'i.

When a husband adds adjectives like 'severe' or 'long' to the word talaq, the meaning of permanence is implied. The Hanafi school primarily treats such descriptions as indicating a complete severance (ba'in). This lesson examines the reasoning behind the majority view (Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad) and the intra-madhhab disagreement with Imam Abu Yusuf, who considers these attributes inappropriate for talaq and thus ineffective.

Guided Path
1
Identify the wording and the majority ruling
The husband says 'anti taliq shadida' or similar. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, this results in one ba'in talaq.
The phrase is treated as a complete issuance.
2
Understand the logical link (talil)
The attribute 'shadida' (severe) or 'arida' (wide) describes something that cannot be retrieved. In talaq, the only type that is irretrievable is ba'in.
The analogy is from common usage: a difficult matter is called 'long and wide'.
3
Note Abu Yusuf's objection
He argues that these attributes are suitable only for physical objects, not for the abstract concept of talaq, so they are لغو (ignored). The talaq becomes raj'i.
Abu Yusuf's proof: attributes of bodies cannot apply to accidents.
4
Apply the principle of intention
If the husband intended three talaqs, his intention is valid because bainunah can be divided into lesser and greater. The intended effect (three) takes precedence.
The majority view is mufta bihi.

ہو گئیں۔ تشریح چونکہ نکاح دخول کیلئے ہوتا ہے۔ اسلئے طلاق بعد الدخول اصل ہے۔ اور قبل الدخول خلاف اصل ہے۔ مصنف ہدایہ نے اصل کو پہلے بیان فرمایا ہے۔ اور خلاف اصل کو بعد میں ۔ مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے اپنی بیوی سے قبل الدخول انت طالق ثلثا کہا تو تینوں طلاقیں واقع ہو جائیں گی ۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ سابق میں گذر چکا کہ جب وصف طلاق عدد کے ساتھ ملا کر ذکر کیا جائے تو طلاق عدد سے واقع ہوگی نہ کہ وصف ہے۔ کیونکہ وقوع طلاق در حقیقت مصدر محذوف سے ہوتا ہے۔ اور یہ عدد اس کی صفت واقع ہو گا۔ پس انت طالق ثلاثاً کے معنی ہوں گے انت طالق طلاقا ثلاثا۔ پس انت طالق سے حدہ طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی۔ بلکہ طلاقاً خلافا سے یکبارگی تین طلاقیں واقع ہو جائیں گی۔
From 'you are divorced a severe, wide, or long divorce' one ba'in talaq will occur. And if he says 'you are divorced a severe, wide, or long divorce', it is one ba'in because what cannot be retrieved is severe for him, and that is ba'in. And what is difficult to retrieve is called a long and wide matter. And from Abu Yusuf it is narrated that by these words raj'i talaq occurs, because this attribute does not befit talaq, so it is لغو. And if he intends three in these sections, his intention is valid due to the division of bainunah as we have passed; what occurs is ba'in. Translation: And if he said 'you are divorced a severe, wide, or long divorce', it is one ba'in. Because the talaq whose retrieval is not possible is severe for the husband, and that is ba'in. And that whose retrieval is difficult is called a long and wide matter. And from Abu Yusuf it is narrated that from these words raj'i talaq occurs, because this attribute is not suitable for talaq, so it is لغو. And if he intends three in all these cases, his intention is correct due to the division of bainunah, and what occurs from these words is ba'in. Explanation: The issue is that if the husband mentions the attribute 'severe' or 'long' or 'wide' with talaq, then ba'in talaq occurs. The proof is that the talaq which is difficult and severe for the husband, whose retrieval via raj'a etc. is not possible, and it is obvious that this can only be achieved by ba'in talaq. For this reason, the ruling of bainunah is given from these words. And a difficult matter whose retrieval is not possible is called a long and wide matter. From Abu Yusuf there is one narration that from these words raj'i talaq occurs. The proof is that this attribute (severity etc.) is not suitable for talaq, because these attributes are qualities of bodies, and talaq is from the category of accidents. Therefore this attribute is لغو, and from 'anti taliq' raj'i talaq occurs. And from 'anti ba'in' until here, in all cases if he intends three talaqs, three occur. Because bainunah is of two types: severe bainunah and light bainunah. So when this person intended three, it is as if he intended the severe bainunah from the two. And intending the effect of one's speech is valid. Therefore intending three talaqs is valid. And Allah knows best. Section on divorce before consummation: The ruling of giving three talaqs before consummation. Chapter on talaq before consummation: When a man divorces his wife three times before consummation with her, they all fall upon her, because what occurs is from a deleted source, because its meaning is 'three talaqs' as we have explained. So his statement 'anti taliq' does not become a separate issuance; thus they all fall together. Translation: This chapter is about divorce before consummation. And when a man divorces his wife before consummation, then all fall upon her. Because what occurs is from a deleted source, because its meaning is 'talaqan thalatha' as we have explained. So his statement 'anti taliq' is not a separate issuance; therefore all three talaqs fall at once. Explanation: Since marriage is for consummation, talaq after consummation is the norm, and before consummation is contrary to the norm. The author of Hidayah mentioned the norm first and the contrary later. The issue is that if someone says to his wife before consummation 'anti taliq thalatha', all three talaqs fall. The proof is that it has passed earlier that when talaq is mentioned with a number, talaq occurs according to the number, not as an attribute. Because the occurrence of talaq in reality is from a deleted source, and this number becomes its attribute. So 'anti taliq thalathan' means 'anti taliq talaqan thalatha'. So from 'anti taliq' alone, one talaq does not occur; rather from 'talaqan thalatha' three talaqs occur at once.
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This passage combines two rulings. First, the ruling on talaq qualified by 'shadida' (severe), 'arida' (wide), or 'tawila' (long). The majority view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that these attributes imply a talaq that is irreparable, i.e., ba'in, because such attributes describe a difficulty that cannot be reversed. Abu Yusuf has a narration that these attributes are appropriate only for physical objects, not for talaq (which is an accident), so they are ignored and raj'i talaq occurs. However, if the husband intends three talaqs, it is valid because bainunah is divisible into lesser (ba'in) and greater (three). Second, the rule on talaq before consummation: if a man says 'anti taliq thalatha' before consummation, all three fall at once. The reasoning: the phrase is interpreted as 'anti taliq talaqan thalatha', meaning the number qualifies the implied source (masdar mahzuf), so the talaq occurs according to the number, not as a separate word. This is consistent with the earlier principle that when talaq is linked to a number, the number governs.

Key Terms
مصدر محذوف (masdar mahzuf): A deleted verbal noun (source) that is implied, e.g., in 'anti taliq thalathan' the word 'talaqan' is omitted but understood. The talaq occurs from that implied source.
بینونت غلیظہ (bainunah ghalizah): Severe bainunah: three talaqs causing complete irrevocable separation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view, a husband says 'anti taliq shadida'. What type of talaq occurs?
A) One raj'i talaq
B) One ba'in talaq
C) Three talaqs
D) No talaq

Key Takeaway
When a husband uses descriptors of severity with talaq, the default ruling is one ba'in talaq, unless he intended three.

Talaq — Divorce

Triple Talaq Before Consummation: All Three Fall at Once
Ruling on triple talaq before consummation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why saying 'anti taliq thalatha' before consummation results in three talaqs, using the Hanafi concept of masdar mahzuf.

Core Idea
Before consummation, saying 'anti taliq thalatha' means three talaqs fall at once due to the implied source (masdar mahzuf).

In Hanafi fiqh, when a husband divorces his wife before consummation with the words 'anti taliq thalatha', the number is not mere description but specifies the count. This lesson unpacks the linguistic reasoning behind the rule that all three talaqs occur simultaneously, and why this is consistent with the principles of talaq.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the phrase 'anti taliq thalatha' as a numerical qualification
The word 'thalatha' (three) is attached to the talaq utterance. It is not a separate sentence but part of the same issuance.
The phrase is one complete sentence.
2
Apply the principle of masdar mahzuf (implied verbal noun)
The phrase means 'anti taliq talaqan thalatha' (you are divorced three talaqs). The word 'talaqan' is omitted but understood. The number qualifies this implied source.
This is a standard Hanafi grammatical analysis.
3
Conclude that the number governs the count
Since the number qualifies the implied source, the talaq occurs according to the number (three), not as a separate utterance. Therefore, three talaqs fall at once.
The ruling applies equally before and after consummation.

Commentary
This passage combines two rulings. First, the ruling on talaq qualified by 'shadida' (severe), 'arida' (wide), or 'tawila' (long). This is consistent with the earlier principle that when talaq is linked to a number, the number governs.

Divorce with Adjectives of Severity: The Hanafi Position and Abu Yusuf's Dissent
States ruling on descriptive adjectives with divorce and Abu Yusuf's dissent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on describing talaq as 'severe', 'broad', or 'long', and explain why Abu Yusuf dissents and which position is mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Describing divorce as 'severe' makes it irrevocable (bain), because only a bain divorce is truly severe.

When a husband says 'I divorce you severely' or 'with a long divorce', does the adjective change the nature of the divorce? This passage presents a dispute within the Hanafi school: the relied-upon position holds that such adjectives produce a bain (irrevocable) divorce, while Abu Yusuf, in one narration, treats them as meaningless, resulting in a raj'i (revocable) divorce. Understanding this dispute helps you grasp how Hanafi scholars weigh linguistic usage and intention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the adjectives and the ruling
Read the passage and note which adjectives (shadid, arid, tawil) are used. The primary ruling states that saying 'anti taliq shadidan' etc. results in one bain divorce.
The adjectives all imply severity or difficulty.
2
Understand the Hanafi proof (talil)
The passage gives a reason: a divorce that cannot be remedied by ruju' is severe, and that is exactly bain divorce. Thus the adjective is given effect because it reflects the husband's intent of finality.
This is a ta'lil (reasoning) linking the adjective's meaning to the legal consequence.
3
Identify Abu Yusuf's contrary view
Abu Yusuf argues that these adjectives are attributes of bodies (ajsam), while divorce is an accident (arad), so the description is inappropriate and should be ignored. Thus the divorce remains raj'i.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; note it is only one narration from Abu Yusuf.
4
Analyse the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
If bain, the husband cannot take his wife back during iddah without a new marriage contract. If raj'i, he may revoke with just two witnesses anytime during iddah.
This difference has direct impact on the couple's situation.
5
Determine the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position
The passage presents the bain ruling as the primary view (from Zahir al-Riwayah), and the later tarjih upholds it. This is the operative position for fatwa.
Remember: the weight of Zahir al-Riwayah supports the bain view.

۲۸۲
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد چهارم ترجمہ اور اگر کہا انت طائق تطلیقہ شدید یا تطبیقہ عریضہ یا تطلیقہ طویلہ تو یہ ایک بائنہ ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ طلاق جسکا تدارک ممکن نہ ہو شوہر پر سخت ہوگی۔ اور وہ بائن ہے۔ اور وہ جس کا تدارک دشوار ہو اس کو کہا جاتا ہے کہ یہ لمبا چوڑا کام ہے۔ اور ابو یوسف سے روایت ہے کہ ان الفاظ سے طلاق رجعی واقع ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ یہ وصف طلاق کے مناسب نہیں ہے۔ لہذا لغو ہوگا۔ اور گران تمام صورتوں میں تین کی نیست کی تو اس کی نیت صحیح ہوگی۔ بینونت کے منقسم ہونے کی وجہ سے اور ان الفاظ سے جو واقع ہوگی وہ بائن ہے۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہاگر شوہر نے طلاق کے ساتھ وصف شدید یا طویل یا عریض ذکر کر دیا تو اس سے طلاق بائن واقع ہوگی۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ شوہر پر وہ طلاق شاق اور صحت ہو گی۔ جس کا تدارک رجعت وغیرہ سے ممکن نہ ہو اور ظاہر ہے کہ یہ بات طلاق بائن سے حاصل ہو سکتی ہے۔ اس وجہ سے ان کلمات سے بینونت کا حکم لگایا گیا ہے اور دشوار کام جس کا تدارک ممکن نہ ہو۔ اس کے بارے میں کہا جاتا ہے کہ یہ کام لمبا چوڑا ہے۔
ابو یوسف سے ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ ان الفاظ سے طلاق رجعی واقع ہو گی۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ وصف (شدت وغیرہ) طلاق کے مناسب نہیں۔ کیونکہ یہ اوصاف صفات اجسام میں سے ہیں۔ اور طلاق اعراض کے قبیل سے ہے ۔ لہذا یہ وصف لغو ہو گا اور انت طالق سے طلاق رجعی واقع ہو جائے گی اور انت بائن سے لے کر یہاں تک تمام صورتوں میں اگر تین طلاق کی نیت کی تو تین واقع ہو جائیں گی ۔ کیونکہ بیونت کی دوقسمیں ہیں۔ بینونت غلیظہ اور بینونت خفیفہ پس جب اس شخص نے تین کی نیت کی تو گویا دونوں میں سے بینوت غلیظہ کی نیت کی ہے۔ اور اپنے کلام کے عمل کی نیت کرنا صحیح ہے۔ اسلئے تین طلاقوں کی نیت صحیح ہو گی ۔ واللہ اعلم
And if he said: 'You are divorced with a severe divorce' or 'a broad divorce' or 'a long divorce', then this is one bain. Because that divorce whose remedy is not possible will be hard on the husband and it is bain. And that which is difficult to remedy is called a lengthy affair. And from Abu Yusuf it is narrated that with these words, a raj'i divorce occurs, because this description is not appropriate for divorce, so it is futile. And in all these cases, if he intended three, his intention is valid because bainunah is divided (into two types), and from these words what occurs is bain. Explanation: The issue is that if the husband mentions a description like severe, long, or broad along with divorce, then a bain divorce occurs. The proof is that the divorce which cannot be remedied by return (ruju') etc. is severe for the husband, and this is achieved by bain divorce. Therefore, the ruling of bainunah is given from these words. And a difficult task which cannot be remedied is said to be lengthy. From Abu Yusuf there is a narration that with these words a raj'i divorce occurs. His proof is that this description is not appropriate for divorce because these are attributes of bodies, while divorce is from accidents. So the description is futile, and from 'anti taliq' a raj'i divorce occurs. And from 'anti bain' up to here, in all cases if he intended three divorces, they all occur because bainunah has two types: severe bainunah and light bainunah. So when this person intended three, he intended severe bainunah. And intending the operation of one's speech is valid. Therefore the intention of three divorces is valid. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of describing divorce with adjectives such as 'severe' (shadid), 'broad' (arid), or 'long' (tawil). The ruling from the Zahir al-Riwayah is that such descriptions render the divorce bain (irrevocable), because the husband emphasizes the severity and finality, which is only achieved by bain divorce. Abu Yusuf, in one narration, holds that the description is inappropriate for divorce (since divorce is an accident, not a body), so it is ignored and the divorce is raj'i (revocable). The commentator also notes that in all these cases, if the husband intends three divorces, that intention is valid because bainunah is divisible: bainunah sughra (light) and bainunah kubra (severe). By intending three, he intends the severe type, and giving effect to one's words through intention is valid.

Key Terms
بائن (bain): Irrevocable divorce; husband cannot revoke it during iddah.
رجعی (raj'i): Revocable divorce; husband may take his wife back during iddah without a new contract.
شديد (shadid): Severe/intense; used as an adjective for talaq indicating finality.
عريض (arid): Broad/wide; used as an adjective for divorce implying difficulty.
طويل (tawil): Long; used as an adjective for divorce implying lengthy difficulty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, if a husband says 'anti taliq shadidatan', what type of divorce occurs?
A) One raj'i divorce
B) One bain divorce
C) Three bain divorces
D) No divorce

Key Takeaway
Adjectives of severity (shadid, arid, tawil) with talaq make it bain (irrevocable) according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Three Divorces Before Consummation: The Linguistic Basis
Ruling on triple talaq before consummation with linguistic proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a triple talaq before consummation falls as three divorces and explain the linguistic argument of the deleted infinitive (masdar mahdhuuf).

Core Idea
Three divorces before consummation all fall together because the number qualifies the implied infinitive, making it one pronouncement.

In Hanafi law, the ruling on triple talaq before consummation hinges on a subtle but critical grammatical insight. When a husband says 'anti taliq thalatha,' it is interpreted as 'anti taliq talaqan thalathan' – you are divorced with three divorces. Because the word 'talaq' (divorce) is implied (masdar mahdhuuf) and the number 'thalatha' describes that implied noun, the entire phrase constitutes a single pronouncement of three divorces, not three separate pronouncements. This lesson unpacks that reasoning and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
State the scenario: a husband says 'anti taliq thalatha' to his wife before consummation. According to the Hanafi school, all three divorces fall instantly, resulting in bainunah kubra (irrevocable separation).
This is the zahir al-riwayah position.
2
Understand the linguistic structure
Recognize that the phrase is parsed as 'anti taliq talaqan thalathan' – the word 'talaq' (divorce) is the deleted infinitive (masdar mahdhuuf) that actually occurs, and 'thalatha' is its description. Thus, the number qualifies the act of divorcing, not the pronouncement itself.
This analysis is drawn from earlier discussions in al-Hidayah.
3
Trace the consequence
Since the number qualifies the implied infinitive, the phrase 'anti taliq thalatha' is a single statement conveying three divorces. There is no separate pronouncement of one divorce, then another, leading to all three occurring simultaneously.
If the husband had said 'anti taliq, anti taliq, anti taliq' separately, the ruling would be different (each is a separate pronouncement).
4
Note the cross-madhhab dispute
Some other schools (e.g., the view attributed to Ibn Abbas and the Dhahiri school) hold that only one divorce falls before consummation, arguing that the absence of consummation lessens the effect of divorce. The Hanafi school rejects this based on the linguistic principle and the generality of the husband's intention.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is that the wife becomes permanently forbidden under the Hanafi view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ترجمہ ( یہ ) فصل (عورت کے ساتھ ) دخول سے پہلے طلاق دینے کے ( بیان ) میں ہے اور جب مرد نے اپنی بیوی کو طلاق دی اس کے ساتھ دخول سے پہلے تو اس پر سب واقع ہو جائیں گی۔ کیونکہ واقع ہونے والا تو مصدر محذوف ہے۔ اسلئے کہ اسکے معنی ہیں طلاقاً ثلاثاً ہم اس کو بیان کر چکے ہیں ۔ پس اس کا قول انت طالق علیحدہ ایقاع نہیں ہوگا۔ لہذا اسب طلاقیں یکباری واقع ہو گئیں۔ تشریح چونکہ نکاح دخول کیلئے ہوتا ہے۔ اسلئے طلاق بعد الدخول اصل ہے۔ اور قبل الدخول خلاف اصل ہے۔ مصنف ہدایہ نے اصل کو پہلے بیان فرمایا ہے۔ اور خلاف اصل کو بعد میں ۔
مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے اپنی بیوی سے قبل الدخول انت طالق ثلثا کہا تو تینوں طلاقیں واقع ہو جائیں گی ۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ سابق میں گذر چکا کہ جب وصف طلاق عدد کے ساتھ ملا کر ذکر کیا جائے تو طلاق عدد سے واقع ہوگی نہ کہ وصف ہے۔ کیونکہ وقوع طلاق در حقیقت مصدر محذوف سے ہوتا ہے۔ اور یہ عدد اس کی صفت واقع ہو گا۔ پس انت طالق ثلاثاً کے معنی ہوں گے انت طالق طلاقا ثلاثا۔ پس انت طالق سے حدہ طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی۔ بلکہ طلاقاً خلافا سے یکبارگی تین طلاقیں واقع ہو جائیں گی۔
Chapter on divorce before consummation. And when a man divorces his wife three times before consummation, they all fall upon her, because what occurs is from a deleted infinitive, since its meaning is three divorces, as we have explained. So his statement 'anti taliq' is not a separate effective pronouncement; thus they all occur together. Translation: This chapter is about divorce before consummation. And when a man divorces his wife three times before consummation, all (three) fall upon her, because the occurring is from a deleted infinitive. Its meaning is three divorces, as we have explained. So his utterance 'anti taliq' is not a separate effective pronouncement, so all three divorces occur at once. Explanation: Since marriage is for consummation, divorce after consummation is the original, and before consummation is contrary to the original. The author of Hidayah mentioned the original first and then the contrary. The issue is that if someone said to his wife before consummation 'anti taliq thalatha', all three divorces occur. The proof is that it has been established earlier that when a description of divorce is mentioned together with a number, the divorce occurs by the number, not by the description. Because the occurrence of divorce is in reality from a deleted infinitive, and this number becomes its description. So 'anti taliq thalathan' means 'you are divorced with three divorces.' Thus from 'anti taliq' alone no divorce occurs; rather from the implied infinitive, three divorces occur all at once.
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on triple talaq before consummation. According to the Hanafi school, if a husband says 'anti taliq thalatha' before consummation, all three divorces fall immediately. The reason is that the phrase is interpreted as 'anti taliq talaqan thalathan' – that is, the word 'talaq' (divorce) is implicit (masdar mahfudh), and the number 'thalatha' qualifies that implicit noun. Thus, it is a single pronouncement of three divorces, not a separate pronouncement of one divorce plus a separate number. The commentator notes that divorce after consummation is the norm (asl), and the author of Al-Hidayah dealt with that first; divorce before consummation is exceptional and treated later. The key point is that because the number is attached to the implied infinitive, all three become effective at once, not sequentially.

Key Terms
مصدر محذوف (masdar mahdhuuf): A deleted infinitive; in Arabic grammar, the action noun is implied and its description (like number) takes effect.
دخول (dukhul): Consummation of marriage; sexual intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) One raj'i divorce
C) Three divorces at once
D) No divorce until consummation

Key Takeaway
Three divorces before consummation fall immediately because the number qualifies the implied infinitive, not the explicit verb.

Sequential Talaq Before Consummation: Only the First Counts
Explains that separate pronouncements of talaq before consummation only effect the first.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of sequential talaq before consummation to determine which pronouncements are effective and which are void.

Core Idea
Before consummation, only the first separate talaq takes effect; subsequent ones are void because the marriage no longer exists to receive them.

This lesson examines what happens when a husband pronounces talaq in separate, unconnected phrases before consummation. The Hanafi school draws a clear line: once the first talaq is effective, the wife becomes bain (irrevocably divorced) and ceases to be a valid subject for further talaq. Understanding this rule requires grasping the concept of mahall (the domain for divorce) and the effect of tafriq (separate pronouncements).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is pronouncing multiple 'taliq' words separately before consummation. The ruling: only the first is effective, making the wife bain; the second and third are void.
The hukm level: bain (irrevocable divorce) for the first; no effect for later ones.
2
Understand the key concept: mahall
For a talaq to take effect, the woman must be in a valid marriage (mahall). After the first bain divorce before consummation, she is no longer a wife, so no mahall remains for subsequent talaqs.
This is a core principle: talaq requires an existing marriage.
3
Distinguish tafriq from linked pronouncements
Tafriq means each 'taliq' is independent. If there is no condition at the end that changes the beginning (e.g., 'in dakhalti al-dar'), then each is separate. If such a condition exists, all may occur together upon fulfillment.
This is a crucial distinction for application.
4
Apply the rule to a concrete scenario
Given 'anti taliq, taliq, taliq' without condition, the first occurs immediately, making her bain. The second and third encounter her while she is bain and thus have no effect.
Remember: she also has no iddah since there was no consummation, so she is entirely free after the first talaq.
5
Note the proof (talil) from the commentator
The proof is based on the nature of independent pronouncements and the disappearance of mahall. The author uses a premise: if a condition is added at the end that changes the beginning, then all may fall together. Without such a condition, each is separate.
This is a reasoning (talil) based on the structure of speech.

ترجمہ . پس اگر اس نے طلاق کو متفرق کیا تو پہلی سے بائنہ ہو گئی اور دوسری سے تیسری واقع نہیں ہوئی اور یہ مثلاً کہے انت طالق ، طالق ، طالق ، کیونکہ ان میں سے ہر ایک علیحدہ ایقاع ہے۔ کیونکہ اپنے کلام کے آخر میں اپنے ایسا کلمہ ذکر نہیں کیا جو صد کلام کو بدل ڈالے۔ یہاں تک کہ (واقع ہونا ) اس امر پر موقوف ہے پس پہلی فی الحال واقع ہو جائے گی۔ پھر دوسری اس کو پہنچے گی درانحالیکہ وہ بائنہ ہے۔

That is like if he says 'anti taliq, taliq, taliq', because each is a separate pronouncement, since he did not mention at the end of his speech something that changes its beginning, so that it depends on that. So the first occurs immediately, then the second encounters her while she is bain. Translation: So if he separated the divorce, then she becomes bain with the first, and the second and third do not occur. For example, he says 'anti taliq, taliq, taliq', because each is a separate pronouncement, since he did not mention at the end of his speech something that changes its beginning, such that (the occurrence) depends on it. So the first occurs immediately, then the second reaches her while she is bain. Explanation: The issue is that if he separates the three divorces, for example he says 'anti taliq, taliq, taliq', then from the first word of divorce she becomes bain, and the second and third do not occur because there is no domain left for them to occur; therefore these two words become futile. From the author of Hidayah's proof, first bear in mind that if he separates the three divorces and at the end of his speech there is a condition or exception that changes the beginning, then in that case even for an unconsummated wife, three divorces occur. For example, he says to his unconsummated wife 'anti taliq, taliq, taliq in dakhalti al-dar', then upon entry into the house, all three divorces occur simultaneously. After this premise, the gist of the proof is that in 'anti taliq taliq taliq', each is a separate pronouncement because there is nothing at the end of the speech that changes the beginning such that the beginning depends on it. So from the first word 'taliq', divorce occurs immediately. Then the second and third occur while the woman has already become bain. And such a bain woman upon whom iddah is not even obligatory is not a domain for divorce.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage addresses the scenario where a husband pronounces divorce in separate, unconnected statements before consummation. The ruling is that only the first divorce takes effect, making the wife bain, and subsequent pronouncements fail because the marriage no longer exists to receive them. The key distinction is whether the later pronouncements are separate (tafriq) or linked by a condition at the end that makes the entire sentence dependent. If there is a condition like 'if you enter the house' at the end, then all three occur simultaneously upon fulfillment of the condition. But if no such backward reference exists, each word is an independent pronouncement, and once the first bain divorce occurs, the woman ceases to be a wife, so further talaqs are inoperative. The commentator clarifies that she becomes bain and, being before consummation, has no iddah, therefore she is not a proper subject for further divorce.

Key Terms
تفرق (tafriq): Separation; pronouncing divorces individually without connection.
محل (mahall): Subject/domain; the wife must be in a valid marriage for divorce to take effect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Three divorces at once
B) One bain divorce
C) One raj'i divorce
D) No divorce

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, before consummation, only the first separate talaq is effective; subsequent ones are void due to the loss of mahall.

Ruling on 'Wahidatan wa Wahidatan' and Death Before Completing Talaq Count
Ruling on sequential 'one and one' and death before completing count

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a husband says 'anti taliq wahidatan wa wahidatan' and when the wife dies before the husband completes the number of divorces.

Core Idea
When 'one and one' is said, only one divorce falls; if the wife dies before the number is completed, no divorce occurs.

In this passage, the author clarifies two scenarios involving the pronouncement of divorce with numbers. First, when a husband says 'you are divorced one and one', only one divorce occurs because the first makes her bain. Second, if the husband begins to say 'you are divorced one' but the wife dies before he utters the final number, no divorce takes effect. The key principle is that the number is the operative element; without it, the pronouncement fails.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Read the passage to find the two cases: (1) 'anti taliq wahidatan wa wahidatan' and (2) 'anti taliq wahidatan' followed by the wife's death before saying the second 'wahidatan'.
Both involve the number determining the effect.
2
Analyze the first scenario
Understand that 'wahidatan wa wahidatan' results in one divorce because the first 'wahidatan' immediately makes her bain. The second 'wa wahidatan' finds her already bain and therefore has no effect.
This shows the sequential nature of the pronouncement.
3
Analyze the second scenario
When the husband says 'anti taliq wahidatan' intending to add another 'wahidatan' but she dies before he speaks, the entire statement is void. The reason is that the number (here 'wahidatan' as the intended second) is the operative element, and death removes the capacity to be divorced.
The husband's incomplete pronouncement is treated as no divorce.
4
Generalize to other numbers
The passage equates this to saying 'ithnatayn' or 'thalathan' – the number governs the effect. If the number is not fully uttered, no divorce occurs.
This reinforces that the number is essential.

Ruling on Separate Divorces for a Non-Consummated Wife
Ruling on three separate divorce pronouncements on ghayr madkhul biha

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on three separate divorce pronouncements to a non-consummated wife, explain the proof based on the concept of mahall, and distinguish the exceptional case where a condition links the pronouncements.

Core Idea
Only the first of three separate divorces takes effect on a non-consummated wife; the rest are void for lack of a valid subject.

In this lesson, we examine a classic Hanafi ruling from the Kitab al-Talaq. When a husband pronounces three divorces separately to a wife with whom he has not consummated the marriage, only the first divorce is effective. The second and third fail because after the first, the wife becomes ba'in and is no longer a valid subject (mahall) for further divorces. Understanding this ruling hinges on the concept of iqa' and the condition of mahall.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is three separate divorce pronouncements (mutafarriq) on a non-consummated wife (ghayr madkhul biha). The ruling: only the first takes effect, making her ba'in; the second and third are null.
This only applies when the divorces are not linked by a condition or exception.
2
Understand the proof: each is an independent iqa'
Each utterance is a separate legal act. Since no condition or exception connects them, the first occurs immediately. After the first, the wife is no longer a legal subject (mahall) for divorce because she is ba'in and has no 'iddah.
The absence of a mahall renders subsequent pronouncements ineffective.
3
Recognize the exceptional case
If the husband attaches a condition (e.g., 'if you enter the house') or an exception that makes the entire speech one integrated statement, then all three divorces occur simultaneously upon fulfillment of the condition.
In that case, the first does not go into effect independently; the whole is a single conditional iqa'.
4
Compare the opposite scenario (consummated wife)
For a consummated wife (madkhul biha), the first divorce is raj'i (revocable) and she remains in 'iddah, so she remains a mahall. Therefore, three separate pronouncements would count as three divorces, making her ba'in after the third.
The key difference is the existence of 'iddah and thus a continuing mahall.

Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi ruling regarding a non-consummated wife (ghayr madkhul biha) when the husband pronounces three divorces in a disconnected manner (mutafarriqan). The ruling is that only the first divorce takes effect, making her ba'in (irrevocably divorced), and the subsequent two are void. The proof provided is that each pronouncement is an independent legal act (iqa'). Since the husband did not attach a condition or exception that would link them together, the first divorce occurs immediately. Once the wife is ba'in, she is no longer legally a wife, especially since a non-consummated wife has no 'iddah period. Therefore, the second and third pronouncements find no subject (mahall) upon which to operate. The text also clarifies an exception: if the husband's speech includes a condition or exception that relates back to the beginning (e.g., 'if you enter the house'), then all three divorces occur upon fulfillment of the condition, as they are considered one integrated statement. This exception is a subtle but important distinction that preserves the integrity of the husband's intent when expressed in a conditional form. The commentary follows the order of the original Arabic text, first stating the ruling, then giving the example, then providing the rational proof, and finally addressing the exception.

Key Terms
مُفَرَّق (mutafarraq): Separate pronouncements of divorce without connecting words or conditions.
بَائِن (ba'in): Irrevocable divorce that ends the marriage immediately without possibility of revocation.
مَحَلّ (mahall): The legal subject upon which a ruling operates; here, the wife as a valid recipient of divorce.
إيقاع (iqa'): The act of effecting or pronouncing a divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Two

Key Takeaway
For a non-consummated wife, only the first of separate divorce pronouncements is valid; the second and third are void because the wife is no longer a legal subject for divorce.

Numbered Divorces with 'Wa' and Death Before Number Completion
Ruling on divorces connected with 'wa' and death before completing the number

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for two scenarios: (1) saying 'one and one' to a non-consummated wife, and (2) the wife dying before the number is pronounced, and explain why the number governs occurrence.

Core Idea
In divorce with number, the number determines occurrence; the wife must be alive when the number is pronounced.

This lesson builds on the principle that if a husband separates his divorce pronouncements, the first makes the wife irrevocably divorced (ba'in) on the spot. When he connects them with 'wa', the same logic applies. However, if the wife dies before the number is completed, no divorce occurs because the subject (mahall) is lost before the specifying number is uttered. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correct application in cases of divorce with numerical terms.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two distinct scenarios
First scenario: husband says 'anti taliq wahidatan wa wahidatan' (one and one) to his non-consummated wife. Second scenario: husband begins to say 'anti taliq wahidatan' (or thintayn, thalathan) but the wife dies before he completes the number word.
The first scenario focuses on the effect of 'wa' between two numbers; the second on the timing of the wife's death.
2
Understand the principle of number over description
In Hanafi law, when a husband combines the description of divorce (wasf – e.g., the word 'taliq') with a number ('adad), the number is what governs the occurrence of divorce. The mere description does not specify how many divorces take place; the number does.
This is a dalil aqli (rational proof) based on the need for certainty in divorce counts.
3
Apply to the first scenario
The husband says 'one and one'. The first 'one' immediately effects a ba'in divorce because the wife is non-consummated. The second 'one' finds no legal subject (mahall) – she is already divorced – so it is void. Only one divorce occurs.
This is similar to the earlier ruling where separate pronouncements without 'wa' also result in one divorce.
4
Apply to the second (death) scenario
The husband says 'anti taliq' but dies before uttering the number (e.g., 'wahidatan'). Since the number is what completes the iqa', and the mahall (the living wife) is lost when she dies, the divorce never occurs. The speech is void. The same applies to 'thintayn' or 'thalathan'.
The key is that the wife must be alive at the moment the number is spoken for the divorce to take effect.
5
Note the homogeneity (tajanus) with the previous case
The passage states that these three cases (one with 'wa', and the three death-before-number scenarios) are homogeneous in meaning with a prior case (the husband saying 'anti taliq thalathan' to a non-consummated wife). The common principle is that the number determines occurrence. However, they differ in outcome because in the prior case the wife was alive when the number was said, whereas here she dies before the number.
Understanding tajanus helps extend rulings by analogy (qiyas).

The proof has passed before that she becomes ba'in by the first 'wahidatan', so the second 'wahidatan' is void. The second issue: if the husband said to his non-consummated wife 'anti taliq wahidatan', but she died before he said 'wahidatan', or he said 'anti taliq thintayn' and she died before pronouncing 'thintayn', or he said 'anti taliq thalathan' and she died before saying 'thalathan' – in all three cases no divorce occurs, and the husband's speech is void. The proof is that the husband combined the description of divorce with the number, and in the occurrence of divorce, the number is considered, not the description. But when she died before he mentioned the number, the mahall was lost before the iqa' of divorce, so his speech is void and no divorce occurs. And 'wa hadha al-tajanus...' indicates that these three issues are homogeneous in meaning with what precedes. What precedes refers to the issue of the husband saying to his non-consummated wife 'anti taliq thalthaan'. The gist of this similarity is that in the occurrence of divorce, the number is considered, not the description. Hence these three issues are similar to the preceding issue. But there is a difference in their ruling: in the preceding issue, divorce occurs because the number found the woman in the state of being a wife; here it does not occur because the number found her in the state of being dead, which is not a mahall for divorce.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage covers two related rulings. First: if a husband says to his non-consummated wife 'anti taliq wahidatan wa wahidatan' (one and one), only one divorce occurs. The reason is that the first 'one' makes her ba'in immediately, so the second 'one' is void – identical to the previous ruling on separate pronouncements without 'wa'. The second ruling: if the husband says 'anti taliq wahidatan' but the wife dies before he completes the word 'wahidatan', or similarly with 'thintayn' or 'thalathan', no divorce occurs. The explanation is that the husband intended to combine the description of divorce (the word 'taliq') with a specific number. In Hanafi law, when a number is mentioned with divorce, the number governs the occurrence – the divorce is contingent upon specifying how many. If the wife dies before the number is uttered, the subject (mahall) of the divorce – the living wife – is lost. Since the number was never completed, the iqa' (occurrence) never happened. The passage concludes that these cases are homogeneous (tajanus) in meaning with the prior ruling on 'thalathan' but differ in outcome because in the earlier case the wife was alive when the number was mentioned, whereas here she dies before the number. The key principle is that for a divorce to occur, the mahall (the wife) must be present as a legal subject at the time the number is stated.

Key Terms
وَصْف (wasf): The description or quality of divorce (e.g., 'taliq' as the act of divorcing).
عَدَد ('adad): The number that specifies how many divorces are intended.
تَجَانُس (tajanus): Homogeneity or similarity in legal meaning between different cases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One divorce occurs
B) The speech is void and no divorce occurs
C) The divorce occurs if she had heard it
D) It depends on whether he intended divorce

Key Takeaway
When a number is mentioned with divorce, the number governs occurrence, and the wife must be alive when the number is fully uttered.

Divorce Count with Temporal Adverbs: The Pronoun Attachment Rule
Ruling on divorce with temporal adverbs and pronoun attachment rule

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of pronoun attachment to temporal adverbs (zarf) to determine the number of divorces that occur in phrases like 'anti taliq wahidatan qabla wahidatan'.

Core Idea
The pronoun attached to 'before' or 'after' determines which divorce the adverb describes, affecting the count.

In Hanafi fiqh, the precise wording of a divorce pronouncement matters greatly. This lesson examines a subtle grammatical rule: when a husband inserts a temporal adverb like 'qabla' (before) or 'ba'da' (after) between two divorce statements, the presence or absence of a pronoun attached to the adverb changes the legal outcome. We will parse the rule, apply it to four sample phrases, and understand the underlying principle that a divorce spoken in the past tense is effective immediately.

Guided Path
1
Identify the temporal adverb and pronoun attachment
Look at the phrase between the two divorce mentions. Is the adverb (qabla/ba'da) attached to the pronoun ha' (her) or not? For example, 'qablaha' has the pronoun; 'qabla' does not.
The pronoun is ha' al-kinaya.
2
Determine which divorce the adverb describes
Hanafi grammar rule: if the adverb has the pronoun, it describes the latter (second) divorce. If no pronoun, it describes the first. This comes from Arabic usage like 'ja'ani Zaydun qablahu 'Amrun' vs 'ja'a fi Zaydin qabla 'Amrin'.
3
Apply the principle of retrospective effectiveness
A divorce spoken in the past tense (e.g., 'you are divorced before') is treated as occurring immediately, because speech cannot actually be in the past. Thus, if the adverb makes one divorce 'before' and the other 'after', both are deemed to occur at the same moment.
This is the Hanafi principle 'iqa' fi al-madi iqa' fi al-hal'.
4
Count the divorces for the four scenarios
Work through each case: (1) 'qabla wahidatan' (no pronoun) → one divorce; (2) 'ba'daha wahidatan' (pronoun on ba'da) → one divorce; (3) 'qablaha wahidatan' (pronoun on qabla) → two divorces; (4) 'ba'da wahidatan' (no pronoun on ba'da) → two divorces.
In cases with one divorce, the wife becomes ba'in immediately; in two-divorce cases, both take effect at once.
5
Confirm the result for a non-consummated wife
The rulings apply to a non-consummated wife (ghayr madkhul biha). Since she is already ba'in by the first divorce, the second cannot occur unless it is deemed simultaneous as per the rule.
For a consummated wife, similar reasoning would apply but the possibility of raj'ah would be considered; the text assumes non-consummated.

Source Text
