ولوقال أنت طالق واحدة قبل واحدة او بعدها واحدة وقعت واحدة والاصل انه متى ذكر شيئين وادخل بينها حرف الظرف ان قرنها بهاء الكناية كان صفة للمذكور اخر اكقوله جاء ني زيد قبله عمرو وان لم يقرنها بهاء الكناية كانت صفة للمذكورا ولا كقوله جاء فى زيد قبل عمرو و ايقاع الطلاق في الماضي ايقاع في الحال لان الاسناد ليس في وسعه فالقبلية في قوله انت طالق واحدة قبل واحدة صفة للاولى فتبين بالا ولى فلاتقع الثانية والبعدية في قوله بعدها واحدة صفة للاخيرة فحصلت الابانة بالاولى ولوقال انت طالق واحدة قبلها واحدة تقع ثنتان لان القبلية صفة للثانية لاتصالها بحرف الكناية فاقتضى ايقاعها فى الماضى وايقاع الأولى فى الحال غيران الايقاع فى الماضى ايقاع في الحال ايضا فتقترنان فتقعان وكذا اذاقال انت طالق واحدة بعد واحدة تقع ثنتان لان البعدية صفة للاولى فاقتضى ايقاع الواحدة في الحال وايقاع الاخرى قبل هذه فتقترنان
ترجمہ اور اگر ( غیر مدخول بہا) سے کہا انت طالق واحدة قبل واحدة يا بعدها واحدة تو ایک واقع ہوگی۔ اور قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ جب دو نیزوں کو ذکر کیا اور ان دونوں کے درمیان کلمہ ظرف داخل کیا ہے تو اگر کلمہ ظرف کو ھاء کنایہ (ضمیر ) کے ساتھ متصل کیا ہے تو اس وقت
And if he said to a non-consummated wife 'anti taliq wahidatan qabla wahidatan' or 'ba'daha wahidatan', one divorce occurs. The principle is: whenever he mentions two things and inserts a particle of time (zarf) between them, if he connects the particle with the pronoun ha' al-kinaya, it is a description of the latter – like his saying 'ja'ani Zaydun qablahu 'Amrun' (Zayd came to me, before him 'Amr). And if he does not connect it with the pronoun ha', it is a description of the first – like his saying 'ja'a fi Zaydin qabla 'Amrin' (he came to Zayd before 'Amr). And the occurrence of divorce in the past is an occurrence in the present, because attribution (isnad) is not within its capacity. So the 'before-ness' (qabliyya) in his saying 'anti taliq wahidatan qabla wahidatan' is a description of the first, so she becomes ba'in by the first, and the second does not occur. And the 'after-ness' (ba'diyya) in his saying 'ba'daha wahidatan' is a description of the latter, so the separation (ibanah) is achieved by the first. And if he said 'anti taliq wahidatan qablaha wahidatan', two occur, because the 'before-ness' is a description of the second due to its connection with the pronoun, so it requires its occurrence in the past, and the occurrence of the first is in the present. However, occurrence in the past is also occurrence in the present, so they coincide and both occur. Similarly, if he said 'anti taliq wahidatan ba'da wahidatan', two occur, because the 'after-ness' is a description of the first, so it requires one occurrence in the present and the other before it, so they coincide. Translation: And if he said to a non-consummated wife 'anti taliq wahidatan qabla wahidatan' or 'ba'daha wahidatan', one divorce occurs. And the principle is: whenever he mentions two things and inserts a particle of time between them, if he connects the particle with the pronoun ha' al-kinaya, then it is a description of the latter... (the Arabic text continues but the Urdu translation is cut off).
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage deals with a nuanced rule about temporal adverbs (zarf) such as 'qabla' (before) and 'ba'da' (after) when used between two divorce pronouncements. The key is whether the adverb is attached to a pronoun (ha' al-kinaya, e.g., 'qablaha' or 'ba'daha') or not. If attached, the adverb describes the second divorce; if not, it describes the first. The text gives examples from Arabic grammar to illustrate. For divorce, the ruling depends on this attachment: In 'qabla wahidatan' (without pronoun), the 'qabla' describes the first divorce, so the first divorce occurs immediately, making her ba'in, and the second does not occur – total one divorce. In 'ba'daha wahidatan' (with pronoun 'ha'), the 'ba'daha' describes the second divorce, so the first divorce occurs immediately, again making her ba'in, and the second does not occur – also one divorce. However, if the husband says 'qablaha wahidatan' (with pronoun on 'qabla'), then 'qablaha' describes the second divorce, making it as if it occurred before the first. Since the 'before' divorce is considered to have occurred in the past, and the first in the present, both are deemed to occur simultaneously – therefore two divorces occur. Similarly, 'ba'da wahidatan' (without pronoun on 'ba'da') describes the first divorce, so the first occurs now and the second before it? Actually the text says 'ba'da wahidatan' without pronoun: 'ba'da' describes the first, meaning the first is 'after' the second? The reasoning is that 'after-ness' for the first requires the second to occur before it, so both occur. The principle relies on the Hanafi legal fiction that a divorce attributed in the past tense is treated as occurring immediately (since speech cannot actually occur in the past). Thus, when the temporal adverb makes one divorce retroactive, both coincide. The Urdu commentary is incomplete, but the Arabic provides the full rule. The passage illustrates the Hanafi method of using Arabic grammatical rules to derive legal conclusions.

Key Terms
ظرف (zarf): A particle of time or place; here specifically temporal adverbs 'qabla' (before) and 'ba'da' (after).
ھاء کنایہ (ha' al-kinaya): The pronoun 'ha' (her) attached to the particle, indicating the described divorce is the latter.
اسناد (isnad): Attribution of a verb to a subject; here it means the action of divorcing cannot be truly past, so past-tense divorce is treated as present.

B) Two
C) Three
D) None

Key Takeaway
The number of divorces in phrases with temporal adverbs depends on whether the adverb is attached to a pronoun, following a precise grammatical rule unique to Hanafi fiqh.

Divorce with Time Particles for a Non-Consummated Wife
Ruling and linguistic analysis of divorce with numbers and 'before'/'after'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for four scenarios of divorce with 'before' and 'after' for a non-consummated wife and explain how the pronoun 'ha' and the principle of past-tense effectuation determine the number of divorces.

Core Idea
For a non-consummated wife, the pronoun 'ha' on a time particle decides whether one or two divorces occur.

This passage examines the intricate rulings when a husband says 'you are divorced one before one' or similar to a non-consummated wife. The author lays down two key principles: the pronoun connection rule and the rule that effectuating divorce in the past is treated as effectuation in the present. These principles are then applied to four distinct scenarios to determine whether one or two divorces occur. Understanding this requires careful analysis of the temporal relationships and the legal effect of a non-consummated wife becoming ba'in with a single divorce.

Guided Path
1
Review the status of a non-consummated wife
A wife who has not been consummated (ghayr madkhul biha) becomes ba'in (irrevocably divorced) with one divorce and is no longer a valid subject for further divorces. This is foundational to understanding why subsequent divorces in the same statement may be invalid.
2
Identify the two linguistic-legal principles
First principle: When a time particle (qabl/ba'd) is connected to the pronominal 'ha' (ها الكناية), it describes the word that follows; if not connected, it describes the word before it. Second principle: Effectuating divorce by attributing it to the past (iqa' fi al-madi) is legally treated as effectuation in the present (iqa' fi al-haal), because true past effectuation is beyond human capacity.
3
Analyze scenarios without the pronoun
In 'You are divorced one before one' (بدون هاء), 'before' describes the first 'one'. Thus the first divorce occurs immediately, making her ba'in, so the second 'one' is futile. Similarly, 'You are divorced one after one' (بدون هاء) yields one divorce because 'after' describes the first, and the second is deemed to occur before the first (past = present) but still only one occurs because the first makes her ba'in? Actually the text says one occurs. Wait: The text says for 'بعدها واحدة' (with pronoun) it's one divorce? Let's re-check. The passage: 'ولوقال أنت طالق واحدة قبل واحدة او بعدها واحدة وقعت واحدة' So 'بعدها واحدة' with pronoun also yields one? Actually 'بعدها' has the pronoun, but the ruling is one divorce. The explanation: 'بعدها' describes the last, so the ba'in occurs by the first. So both 'قبل واحدة' and 'بعدها واحدة' yield one divorce. The differentiation is between the presence/absence of pronoun on 'قبل' not on 'بعد'? Let's verify: The four cases: (1) واحدة قبل واحدة, (2) واحدة بعدها واحدة, (3) واحدة قبلها واحدة, (4) واحدة بعد واحدة. Cases 1 and 2 yield one divorce; cases 3 and 4 yield two. So case 2 has pronoun on بعد but yields one; case 4 without pronoun on بعد yields two. So it's not simply pronoun=describes latter. Need to be careful: The principle applies to the time particle relative to the two numbers. In 'بعدها واحدة', 'بعدها' describes the last number (الثانية) because of the pronoun, so the last 'واحدة' is described by 'بعد', meaning it occurs after the first. But since it's 'بعدها' (after her), the second occurs after the first? That would make the second invalid because the first made her ba'in. Wait, the author says: 'والبعدية في قوله بعدها واحدة صفة للاخيرة فحصلت الابانة بالاولى' meaning the 'ba'diyyah' is a description of the last (the second), so separation (ba'in) occurs by the first. So the second does not occur because it is after the first. So one divorce. So case 2: 'بعدها واحدة' yields one divorce. Case 4: 'بعد واحدة' without pronoun: 'بعد' describes the first, so the first occurs in the present, and the second before it (past=present), so both concurrent → two. Similarly, 'قبلها واحدة' (case 3) with pronoun: 'قبل' describes the second, so the second occurs before the first (past=present), and the first in present, both concurrent → two. 'قبل واحدة' (case 1) without pronoun: 'قبل' describes the first, so first occurs before the second, but first makes her ba'in, second invalid → one. So the nuance: with pronoun on 'قبل' it describes the second → two; without pronoun on 'قبل' it describes the first → one. With pronoun on 'بعد' it describes the second → one; without pronoun on 'بعد' it describes the first → two. So it's not a simple rule; we need to analyze each case. This is the 'expansion_probe' – we need to walk through carefully. The guided_path should reflect this analysis.
Important: The ruling for 'بعدها واحدة' is one divorce, not two. The pronoun rule works inversely for 'بعد' because 'بعد' indicates subsequence. So we must apply both principles correctly.
4
Apply the principle of past-tense effectuation
When a divorce is deemed to occur 'before' another, it is legally treated as occurring in the present along with the other. This concurrent effectuation is key to understanding how two divorces can occur in cases 3 and 4.
5
Enumerate and verify all four scenarios
List the four cases: (1) واحدة قبل واحدة → 1 divorce, (2) واحدة بعدها واحدة → 1 divorce, (3) واحدة قبلها واحدة → 2 divorces, (4) واحدة بعد واحدة → 2 divorces. Verify each using the principles.

ولوقال أنت طالق واحدة قبل واحدة او بعدها واحدة وقعت واحدة والاصل انه متى ذكر شيئين وادخل بينها حرف الظرف ان قرنها بهاء الكناية كان صفة للمذكور اخر اكقوله جاء ني زيد قبله عمرو وان لم يقرنها بهاء الكناية كانت صفة للمذكورا ولا كقوله جاء فى زيد قبل عمرو و ايقاع الطلاق في الماضي ايقاع في الحال لان الاسناد ليس في وسعه فالقبلية في قوله انت طالق واحدة قبل واحدة صفة للاولى فتبين بالا ولى فلاتقع الثانية والبعدية في قوله بعدها واحدة صفة للاخيرة فحصلت الابانة بالاولى ولوقال انت طالق واحدة قبلها واحدة تقع ثنتان لان القبلية صفة للثانية لاتصالها بحرف الكناية فاقتضى ايقاعها فى الماضى وايقاع الأولى فى الحال غيران الايقاع فى الماضى ايقاع فى الحال ايضا فتقترنان فتقعان وكذا اذاقال انت طالق واحدة بعد واحدة تقع ثنتان لان البعدية صفة للاولى فاقتضى ايقاع الواحدة في الحال وايقاع الاخرى قبل هذه فتقترنان
ترجمہ اور اگر ( غیر مدخول بہا) سے کہا انت طالق واحدة قبل واحدة يا بعدها واحدة تو ایک واقع ہوگی۔ اور قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ جب دو نیزوں کو ذکر کیا اور ان دونوں کے درمیان کلمہ ظرف داخل کیا ہے تو اگر کلمہ ظرف کو ھاء کنایہ (ضمیر ) کے ساتھ متصل کیا ہے تو اس وقت
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد چہارم (اسکی ) صفت ہو گا جو آخر میں مذکور ہے۔ جیسے اس کا قول جاء نی زید قبله عمر - اور گر ظرف کوھا کنایہ کے ساتھ متصل نہیں کیا تو ظرف مذکور اول کی صفت ہو گا۔ جیسے اس کا قول جائی زہد قبل عمرہ ۔ اور طلاق کو ماضی میں واقع کرنا فی الحال واقع کرنا ہے۔ کیونکہ (ماضی کی طرف) نسبت اسکی قدرت میں نہیں ہے۔ پس قبلیت اسکے قول انت طالق واحدة قبل واحدۃ میں اولیٰ کی صفت ہے۔ پس اولی سے بائنہ ہو جائے گی ۔ اور دوسری واقع نہیں ہوگی۔ اور بعدیت اسکے قول بعدها واحدة میں صفت ہے آخیرہ کی۔ لہذا اہانت اولی کے ذریعہ حاصل ہو گئی اور اگر کہا انت طالق واحدة قبلها واحدة تو دو واقع ہوں گی ۔ کیونکہ قبلیت صف ہے ثانیہ کی اس کے متصل ہونے کی وجہ سے حرف کنایہ (ضمیر) کے ساتھ ۔ پس تقاضا کیا ثانیہ کو ماضی میں واقع کرنے کا اور اولیٰ کو فی الحال واقع کرنے کا مگر یہ کہ ایقاع فی الماضى ايقاع فی الحال ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا ( اولی و تانیہ ) دونوں مقترن ہوں گی۔ اور دونوں واقع ہو جائیں گی ۔ اور ایسے ہی جب کہا انت طالق واحدة بعد واحدة تو دود واقع ہوں گی ۔ کیونکہ بعد یت اولیٰ کی صفت ہے۔ پس تقاضا کیا واحدۃ اولی کو واقع کرنے کا فی الحال۔ اور واحدۃ ثانیہ کو اس سے پہلے واقع کرنے گا ۔ لہذا دونوں مقترن ہوں گی۔
تشریح اس عبارت میں طلاق قبل الدخول کی چار صورتیں اور زیر بحثہ ہیں :-
(1
انت طالق واحدة قبل واحدة
(2
انت طالق واحدة بعدها واحدة
(3
انت طالق واحدة قبلها واحدة
(4
انت طالق واحدة بعد واحدة
پہلی دو صورتوں میں ایک طلاق واقع ہوگی۔ اور بعد کی دو صورتیں میں دو طلاقیں واقع ہوں گی۔ نیہ ذہن نشین رکھا جائے کہ لفظ قبل تقدیم کیلئے آتا ہے اور لفظ بعد تا خیر کیلئے۔
یہ چاروں صورتیں دو اصول پر موقوف ہیں، جن کو مصنف نے کتاب میں ذکر فرمایا ہے۔ اول یہ کہ ظرف یعنی لفظ قبل اور بعد جب ھا کنایہ یعنی ضمیر کے ساتھ مقید کیا جائے تو ظرف بعد کیلئے صفت ہو گا۔ اور اگر ھائے کنایہ کے ساتھ مقید نہ کیا جائے تو اپنے ماقبل کی صفت ہو گا ( یہاں صفت سے صفت معنوی مراد ہے نہ کہ صفت نحوی ) اس اصول کی وضاحت ان دو مثالوں سے ہو جائے گی۔ جاءنی زید قبلہ عمرو اور جائنی زید قبل عمر و۔ پہلی مثال میں قبلیت ما بعد یعنی عمر کی صفت ہے۔ مطلب ہو گا عمر کہ پہلے آیا اور زید بعد میں ۔ اور دوسری مثال میں قبلیت ماقبل یعنی زید کی صفت ہے۔ یعنی زید پہلے آیا اور عمر بعد میں۔
دوسرا اصول یہ ہے کہ ایقاع فی الماضی ایقاع فی الحال ہوتا ہے یعنی زمانہ ماضی کی جانب منسوب کر کے اگر طلاق واقع کی جائے تو وہ زمانہ حال میں واقع ہوگی نہ کہ ماضی میں۔ کیونکہ ماضی کی طرف نسبت کرتے ہوئے طلاق واقع کرنا انسان کی قدرت سے خارج ہے۔ یعنی یہ ممکن نہیں کہ کوئی شخص آج انت طالق اس کے ذریعہ طلاق دے اور وہ طلاق کل گذشتہ میں واقع بھی ہو جائے ۔ ان دو اصول کے علاوہ ایک بات اور یادرکھئے وہ یہ کہ غیر مدخول بہا عورت ایک طلاق سے بائن ہو جاتی ہے۔ اور اس پر عدت واجب نہیں ہوتی اور نہ ہی ایک کے بعد محل طلاق رہتی ہے۔ اب اگر کسی نے اپنی غیر مدخول بہا بیوی سے انت طالق واحدة قبل واحدة اس صورت میں لفظ قبل ماقبل کی صفت ہوگا۔ اور معنی یہ ہوں گے کہ واحدہ اولی پہلے واقع ہوئی اور واحدہ ثانیہ بعد میں۔ پس جب واحدہ اولی واقع ہوئی تو غیر مدخول بہا بائنہ ہوگی۔ اور ۔ واحدہ ثانیہ کیلئے محل باقی نہ رہنے کی وجہ سے واحدہ ثانیہ لغو ہوگئی۔ پس ثابت ہوا کہ اس صورت میں ایک واقع ہوگئی اور اگر کہا انت طالف
And similarly when he said 'You are divorced two or three' due to the proof we mentioned. And it is similar in meaning to the preceding. Explanation: If a husband said to his non-consummated wife 'You are divorced one', one ba'in divorce occurs. The proof passed earlier that she becomes ba'in by the first 'one', so the second 'one' is futile. Second issue: If the husband said to his non-consummated wife 'You are divorced one', but she died before saying 'one', or said 'You are divorced two' and she died before pronouncing 'two', or 'You are divorced three' and she died before pronouncing 'three', then in all three cases no divorce occurs and the husband's speech is void. The proof is that the husband attached the attribute of divorce to the number, and in the occurrence of divorce the number is considered not the attribute. But when she died before mentioning the number, the subject was lost before the effectuation of divorce. So his speech is void and no divorce occurs. 'And this similarity...' He says these three issues are similar in meaning to the preceding. Preceding refers to the case where the husband said to his non-consummated wife 'You are divorced three'. The gist of this similarity is that the number is considered in effecting divorce, not the attribute. So these three issues resemble the preceding issue, but their rulings differ because in the preceding issue divorce occurs because the number found the woman in the state of being a wife, while here it does not occur because the number found her in a state of being dead, which is not a subject for divorce. 'You are divorced one before one or after one' – one divorce occurs. And if he said 'You are divorced one before one or after one', one divorce occurs. The principle is that whenever two things are mentioned and a particle of time is inserted between them, if it is connected with the pronominal 'ha', it describes the latter, like his saying 'Zaid came, before him Amr'. If not connected with the pronominal 'ha', it describes the former, like his saying 'Zaid came, before Amr'. Effecting divorce in the past is effecting in the present because attribution is not within his capacity. So 'before' in his saying 'You are divorced one before one' is a description of the first, so she becomes ba'in by the first, and the second does not occur. 'After' in his saying 'after her one' is a description of the last, so the ba'in occurs by the first. If he said 'You are divorced one before her one', two occur because 'before' describes the second due to its connection with the pronominal 'ha', necessitating its effectuation in the past, and the first in the present, but effectuation in the past is also effectuation in the present, so they are concurrent and both occur. Likewise if he said 'You are divorced one after one', two occur because 'after' describes the first, necessitating effectuation of the one in the present and the other before it, so they are concurrent. Translation: And if he said to a non-consummated wife 'You are divorced one before one' or 'after one', one occurs. The rule is that when two matters are mentioned and a time particle is inserted between them, if the particle is connected with the pronominal 'ha', it describes the latter. Like his saying 'Zaid came, before him Amr.' And if not connected with the pronominal 'ha', it describes the former, like his saying 'Zaid came, before Amr.' Effecting divorce in the past is effecting in the present because attribution to the past is not within his power. So 'before' in 'You are divorced one before one' describes the first, so she becomes ba'in by the first, and the second does not occur. 'After' in his saying 'after her one' describes the last, so the ba'in occurs by the first. If he said 'You are divorced one before her one', two occur because 'before' describes the second due to its connection with the pronominal, necessitating its effectuation in the past, and the first in the present, but effectuation in the past is also effectuation in the present, so they are concurrent and both occur. Likewise if he said 'You are divorced one after one', two occur because 'after' describes the first, necessitating effectuation of the one in the present and the other before it, so they are concurrent. Explanation: In this passage, four scenarios of divorce before consummation are under discussion: (1) 'You are divorced one before one' (2) 'You are divorced one after her one' (3) 'You are divorced one before her one' (4) 'You are divorced one after one'. In the first two cases, one divorce occurs; in the latter two, two divorces occur. Note that the word 'before' indicates precedence and 'after' indicates subsequence. These four scenarios depend on two principles mentioned by the author. First: when the particle i.e., 'before' or 'after', is tied with the pronominal 'ha', it describes the latter; if not tied with 'ha', it describes the former (here 'description' means semantic description, not grammatical). Clarification with two examples: 'Zaid came before him Amr' and 'Zaid came before Amr'. In the first, 'before' describes the latter i.e., Amr, meaning Amr came first and Zaid later. In the second, 'before' describes the former i.e., Zaid, meaning Zaid came first and Amr later. Second principle: effecting divorce in the past is effecting in the present – meaning if divorce is attributed to past time, it occurs in the present, not the past, because attributing to the past is beyond human capacity. That is, it is not possible for someone today to say 'you are divorced' and have that divorce occur yesterday. In addition to these two principles, remember that a non-consummated woman becomes ba'in with one divorce, and she does not have an 'iddah, nor does she remain a subject for divorce after one. Now if someone said to his non-consummated wife 'You are divorced one before one', the word 'before' describes the former, meaning the first 'one' occurred first and the second later. When the first 'one' occurred, the non-consummated woman becomes ba'in, so the second 'one' becomes futile due to lack of subject. Thus in this case, one occurs. And if he said 'You are divorced...' Commentary
This passage is a ruling with detailed proof explaining the effect of numbers and time particles in divorce statements directed at a non-consummated wife. The author begins by reaffirming that saying 'you are divorced two' or 'three' follows the same logic as 'one' for a non-consummated wife – but with a crucial distinction: if the wife dies before the number is pronounced, no divorce occurs because the subject (the wife as a wife) is lost before the number completes the effectuation. The core proof is that the number is the operative element (mu'tabar), not the mere description of divorce. The passage then addresses a more complex scenario: when the husband says 'you are divorced one before one' or 'after one' etc. The author lays down a linguistic principle for interpreting such statements: the time particle ('before' or 'after') when connected to a pronoun (ha al-kinaayah) describes the word that follows it; when not connected, it describes the word before it. Applying this to a non-consummated wife: in 'you are divorced one before one', 'before' describes the first 'one', so the first divorce occurs immediately, making her ba'in, and the second 'one' is ineffective because the subject is gone. In 'you are divorced one after her one', 'after' describes the last 'one', but effectuation in the past is effectuation in the present, so both occur simultaneously – but here only one occurs because the first 'one' makes her ba'in and the second is futile? Actually the text says in the first two cases (بدون هاء) one divorce occurs, but in the latter two (with هاء) two occur. The commentary explains that when 'before' is connected to the pronoun ('before her one'), it describes the second divorce, making it occur in the past (which is effectively present), so both divorces are concurrent and two happen. Similarly, 'after one' (without pronoun) describes the first divorce, so the first occurs in the present and the second before it (also present), so both are concurrent. The key principle is that for a non-consummated wife, after one divorce she is no longer a valid subject, so any further divorce within the same statment must be analyzed to see if it occurs before or after the ba'in. Through the linguistic rules, the author determines whether the second divorce is deemed to occur before the first (and thus valid) or after (and invalid). The passage concludes with a clear enumeration of the four cases and their rulings, emphasizing the two foundational principles: the pronoun connection rule and the rule that past-tense effectuation is present-tense effectuation. This is a classic example of Hanafi precision in analyzing conditional and temporal divorce expressions.

Key Terms
عدد ('adad): The number (one, two, three) that is essential for the occurrence of divorce; without it, the attribute (وصف) of divorce alone does not effect a valid divorce.
ها الكناية (haa al-kinaayah): The pronominal 'ha' (her) that connects the time particle to the second divorce word, making the particle describe the latter.
إيقاع في الماضي إيقاع في الحال (iqa' fi al-madi iqa' fi al-haal): Effectuating a divorce by attributing it to the past time is legally treated as effectuation in the present, because true past effectuation is impossible for humans.
غير مدخول بها (ghayr madkhul biha): A wife who has not been consummated; she becomes ba'in (irrevocably divorced) with one divorce and does not observe 'iddah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A non-consummated wife is told 'أنت طالق واحدة بعد واحدة'. How many divorces occur according to the Hanafi school?
A) None, because the statement is contradictory.
B) One divorce, because the first makes her ba'in.
C) Two divorces, because 'بعد' without pronoun describes the first, making the second occur before (past=present), and both are concurrent.
D) Two divorces, because the number two is implied.

Key Takeaway
For a non-consummated wife, the number of divorces in statements with time particles depends on whether the particle is connected to the pronoun 'ha' and on the principle that past-tense effectuation equals present-tense effectuation.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
8 min
Four Scenarios of Talaq with Qabl and Ba'd Before Consummation
Explaining two linguistic principles with four talaq scenarios

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi linguistic principles for qabl and ba'd to determine the number of divorces in four different phrasings before consummation.

Core Idea
When a pronoun connects the adverb, it qualifies the next noun; past-tense divorce works now.

In this passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah, the commentator clarifies how subtle Arabic phrasing affects the counting of divorces before consummation. Two key linguistic rules and a specific Hanafi principle about past-tense divorce are applied to four scenarios. By mastering these rules, you will see how the same formula can yield either one or two divorces based on whether the adverb (qabl/ba'd) is connected to a pronoun.

Guided Path
1
Learn the two principles
First, understand the rule: when the adverb (qabl/ba'd) is connected to a pronoun (e.g., qablaha), it qualifies the following noun; otherwise it qualifies the preceding noun. Second, remember that effecting divorce in past tense actually operates in the present (īqā' fī al-māḍī īqā' fī al-ḥāl).
These are the analytical tools from the source.
2
Identify the phrasing of each scenario
There are four formulas: (1) انت طالق واحدة قبل واحدة (before one), (2) انت طالق واحدة بعدها واحدة (after it one), (3) انت طالق واحدة قبلها واحدة (before it one), (4) انت طالق واحدة بعد واحدة (after one). Note whether the adverb has the pronoun ha or not.
Scenario 1: without pronoun; scenario 2: with pronoun; scenario 3: with pronoun; scenario 4: without pronoun.
3
Apply principle 1 (adverb attribute)
For each scenario, determine which noun the adverb qualifies. Without pronoun: qualifies preceding noun. With pronoun: qualifies following noun. This tells us which divorce is placed earlier/later in the statement.
4
Apply principle 2 (past tense = present)
Any divorce attributed to past time (e.g., second divorce supposedly before first) actually occurs simultaneously with the present-tense divorce. So both are effective together.
This prevents impossible past divorces.
5
Determine the number of effective divorces
For an unconsummated wife, one divorce makes her bain (irrevocable), leaving no place for a second. In scenarios where the second divorce is placed after the first, it is invalid. In scenarios where both are placed simultaneously (due to past-tense rule), two divorcees occur.
Scenarios 1 and 2: one divorce; scenarios 3 and 4: two divorces.

یہ چاروں صورتیں دو اصول پر موقوف ہیں، جن کو مصنف نے کتاب میں ذکر فرمایا ہے۔ اول یہ کہ ظرف یعنی لفظ قبل اور بعد جب ھا کنایہ یعنی ضمیر کے ساتھ مقید کیا جائے تو ظرف بعد کیلئے صفت ہو گا۔ اور اگر ھائے کنایہ کے ساتھ مقید نہ کیا جائے تو اپنے ماقبل کی صفت ہو گا ( یہاں صفت سے صفت معنوی مراد ہے نہ کہ صفت نحوی ) اس اصول کی وضاحت ان دو مثالوں سے ہو جائے گی۔ جاءنی زید قبلہ عمرو اور جائنی زید قبل عمر و۔ پہلی مثال میں قبلیت ما بعد یعنی عمر کی صفت ہے۔ مطلب ہو گا عمر کہ پہلے آیا اور زید بعد میں ۔ اور دوسری مثال میں قبلیت ماقبل یعنی زید کی صفت ہے۔ یعنی زید پہلے آیا اور عمر بعد میں۔
دوسرا اصول یہ ہے کہ ایقاع فی الماضی ایقاع فی الحال ہوتا ہے یعنی زمانہ ماضی کی جانب منسوب کر کے اگر طلاق واقع کی جائے تو وہ زمانہ حال میں واقع ہوگی نہ کہ ماضی میں۔ کیونکہ ماضی کی طرف نسبت کرتے ہوئے طلاق واقع کرنا انسان کی قدرت سے خارج ہے۔ یعنی یہ ممکن نہیں کہ کوئی شخص آج انت طالق اس کے ذریعہ طلاق دے اور وہ طلاق کل گذشتہ میں واقع بھی ہو جائے ۔ ان دو اصول کے علاوہ ایک بات اور یادرکھئے وہ یہ کہ غیر مدخول بہا عورت ایک طلاق سے بائن ہو جاتی ہے۔ اور اس پر عدت واجب نہیں ہوتی اور نہ ہی ایک کے بعد محل طلاق رہتی ہے۔ اب اگر کسی نے اپنی غیر مدخول بہا بیوی سے انت طالق واحدة قبل واحدة اس صورت میں لفظ قبل ماقبل کی صفت ہوگا۔ اور معنی یہ ہوں گے کہ واحدہ اولی پہلے واقع ہوئی اور واحدہ ثانیہ بعد میں۔ پس جب واحدہ اولی واقع ہوئی تو غیر مدخول بہا بائنہ ہوگی۔ اور ۔ واحدہ ثانیہ کیلئے محل باقی نہ رہنے کی وجہ سے واحدہ ثانیہ لغو ہوگئی۔ پس ثابت ہوا کہ اس صورت میں ایک واقع ہوگئی اور اگر کہا انت طالف واحدة بعدها واحدة اس صورت میں لفظ بعد مابعد کی صفت ہوگا۔ معنی یہ ہوں گے کہ تجھ کو ایک طلاق ہے اس کے بعد ایک ہے۔ یعنی واحد و اولی سے غیر مدخول بہا بائنہ ہوگئی۔ اس کے بعد واحدہ ثانی محل طلاق فوت ہونے کی وجہ سے لغو ہو جائے گی ۔ لہذا اس صورت میں بھی ایک ہی واقع ہوگی۔
اور اگر کہا انت طالق واحدة قبلها واحدة اس صورت میں لفظ قبل ما بعد کی صفت ہوگا یعنی تجھ کو ایک طلاق ہے اس سے پہلے ایک ۔ یہ کلام تقاضا کرتا ہے ایقاع ثانیہ کا ماضی میں اور ایقاع اولی کا حال میں اور چونکہ ایقاع فی الماضی ایقاع فی الحال ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا دونوں طلاقیں زمانہ حال میں ساتھ ساتھ واقع ہوں گی اور غیر مدخول بہا بیوی کو یکبارگی دو طلاقیں دی جاسکتی ہیں۔ اسلئے اس صورت میں دو واقع ہوں گی ۔ اور اگر کہا انت طالق واحدة بعد واحد و یعنی تجھ کو ایک طلاق ہے بعد ایک کے اس صورت میں لفظ بعد ماقبل کی صفت ہوگا۔ اور یہ کلام تقاضا کرے گا اولی کو واقع کرنے کا زمانہ حال میں اور ثانیہ کو اولی سے پہلے اور ظاہر ہے کہ اولی کے وقوع سے پہلے کا زمانہ ماضی ہوگا تو گویا کہ ثانیہ کو زمانہ ماضی میں واقع کیا گیا ہے۔ اور چونکہ ایقاع فی الماضی ایقاع فی الحال ہوتا ہے لہذا یہ دونوں طلاقیں زمانہ حال میں ساتھ ساتھ واقع ہوں گی۔ اس وجہ سے اس صورت میں بھی غیر مدخول بہا پر دو واقع ہو جائیں گی۔
This is the commentary Ashraf al-Hidayah, Urdu explanation of Hidayah, volume 4. (Its) attribute will be what is mentioned at the end. Like his saying 'Zaid came to me, before him Amr.' And if the adverb is not connected with the pronoun, then the mentioned adverb will be the attribute of the first. Like his saying 'Zaid came before Amr.' And effecting divorce in the past is effecting it in the present. Because (towards the past) attribution is not within his power. So precedence in his saying 'you are divorced one before one' is the attribute of the first. So with the first she becomes bain. And the second does not occur. And subsequence in his saying 'after it one' is the attribute of the last. Therefore, separation is obtained through the first. And if he said 'you are divorced one before it one', then two occur. Because precedence is the attribute of the second due to its connection with the pronoun. So it requires effecting the second in the past and the first in the present, but effecting in the past is effecting in the present. So both will be simultaneous and both will occur. Similarly, when he said 'you are divorced one after one', two occur. Because subsequence is the attribute of the first. So it requires effecting the first in the present and the second before it. So both will be simultaneous. Explanation: In this phrase, four scenarios of divorce before consummation are under discussion: (1) You are divorced one before one, (2) You are divorced one after it one, (3) You are divorced one before it one, (4) You are divorced one after one. In the first two scenarios, one divorce occurs, and in the last two scenarios, two divorces occur. Keep in mind that the word 'before' comes for advancement and 'after' for delay. These four scenarios are based on two principles which the author mentioned in the book. First: When the adverb, i.e., the word 'before' and 'after', is connected with the pronoun, then the adverb will be an attribute for what follows; and if not connected with the pronoun, it will be an attribute of what precedes. (Here attribute means semantic attribute, not grammatical attribute.) Clarification of this principle will be from these two examples: 'Zaid came to me, before him Amr' and 'Zaid came before Amr'. In the first example, precedence is the attribute of what follows, i.e., Amr; meaning Amr came first and Zaid after. In the second example, precedence is the attribute of what precedes, i.e., Zaid; meaning Zaid came first and Amr after. Second principle: Effecting in the past is effecting in the present; i.e., if divorce is effected by attributing it to past time, it will occur in the present, not in the past, because effecting divorce by attributing it to the past is beyond human power; i.e., it is not possible for a person today to say 'you are divorced' and that divorce occurs yesterday. Besides these two principles, there is another thing to remember: an unconsummated woman becomes bain (irrevocably separated) with one divorce, and 'iddah is not obligatory upon her, nor does she remain a place of divorce after one. Now if someone said to his unconsummated wife 'you are divorced one before one', in this scenario the word 'before' is attribute of what precedes, and the meaning is that the first one occurred earlier and the second one later. So when the first one occurred, the unconsummated woman becomes bain, and due to the absence of the place for divorce, the second becomes invalid. So it is established that in this scenario one occurs. And if he said 'you are divorced one after it one', in this scenario the word 'after' is attribute of what follows; the meaning is you have one divorce and after it one. So by the first one, the unconsummated woman becomes bain, then the second become invalid due to loss of the place. Hence in this scenario also only one occurs. And if he said 'you are divorced one before it one', in this scenario the word 'before' is attribute of what follows, i.e., you have one divorce and before it one. This speech requires effecting the second in the past and the first in the present. And since effecting in the past is effecting in the present, therefore both divorces occur simultaneously in the present time, and an unconsummated wife can be given two divorces at once. So in this scenario two occur. And if he said 'you are divorced one after one', i.e., you have one divorce after one, in this scenario the word 'after' is attribute of what precedes, and this speech will require effecting the first in the present and the second before it. It is obvious that the time before the occurrence of the first is past, so it is as if the second is effected in past time. And since effecting in the past is effecting in the present, therefore both divorces occur simultaneously in the present. Therefore in this scenario also two occur for an unconsummated wife.
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage is a commentary explaining two linguistic principles and their application to four scenarios of divorce (talaq) before consummation. The author begins by stating that when a man mentions an adverb like 'before' or 'after' connected with a pronoun (e.g., 'before it', 'after it'), that adverb qualifies the following noun. If not connected, it qualifies the preceding. Examples from everyday speech clarify: 'Zaid came before him Amr' means Amr came first; 'Zaid came before Amr' means Zaid came first. The second principle is that effecting a divorce in the past tense (e.g., 'you were divorced yesterday') actually operates in the present because one cannot truly cause a past event. This is a key Hanafi rule: al-iqā' fī al-māḍī iqā' fī al-ḥāl. Then the text explains the four formulas: (1) 'you are divorced one before one' – here 'before' qualifies the first divorce, so the first occurs immediately, making her bain (irrevocably divorced), and the second is invalid. (2) 'you are divorced one after it one' – 'after' qualifies the second, so again only one occurs. (3) 'you are divorced one before it one' – 'before' qualifies the second (with pronoun), so the second is placed in the past and the first in the present; but since past=present, both occur at once. (4) 'you are divorced one after one' – 'after' qualifies the first, so the first is in the present, the second is placed before it (i.e., in the past), and again both occur. Thus for an unconsummated wife, scenarios (1) and (2) yield one divorce; (3) and (4) yield two divorces. The commentary follows the author's order: first stating the principles, then listing the four formulas, then applying each formula step by step. It reminds the reader that an unconsummated wife becomes bain with one divorce and cannot receive further divorces, so any additional divorce is invalid unless both occur simultaneously.

Key Terms
قبل (qabl): An adverb meaning 'before'; when connected with a pronoun (qablaha), it qualifies the following noun; without pronoun, it qualifies the preceding.
بعد (ba'd): An adverb meaning 'after'; when connected with a pronoun (ba'daha), it qualifies the following noun; without pronoun, it qualifies the preceding.
صفت (sifat): In this context, 'attribute' (ma'nawi) referring to the semantic relation of the adverb to a noun, not grammatical adjective.
ایقاع فی الماضی (īqā' fī al-māḍī): Effecting a divorce by attributing it to past time; the Hanafi rule is that this actually operates in the present because one cannot truly cause a past event.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man says to his unconsummated wife: 'You are divorced one after it one' (انت طالق واحدة بعدها واحدة). How many divorces occur?
A) Two divorces
B) One divorce
C) None
D) Three divorces

Key Takeaway
The number of divorces in ambiguous phrasings before consummation is determined by two principles: the pronoun attachment rule and the rule that past-tense divorce effects present.

Talaq with 'Ma'a' (With) and the Dispute of Abu Yusuf
Ruling for talaq using 'with' and intra-Hanafi difference

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the majority Hanafi ruling on talaq using 'ma'a' and explain Abu Yusuf's opposing reasoning based on the pronoun's implication of sequence.

Core Idea
When saying 'with it one', the pronoun 'it' triggers a dispute: two divorces at once or one first then invalid.

This lesson examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding the phrase 'you are divorced one with it one' (انت طالق واحدة معها واحدة). The word 'ma'a' (with) normally indicates simultaneity, but the pronoun 'ha' introduces a temporal element. The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) hold that two divorces occur together, while Abu Yusuf argues that the pronoun forces the first to precede, invalidating the second for an unconsummated wife. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to analyze linguistic implications in talaq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the phrase and the two contexts
Note the phrase 'ma'aha wahida' (with it one) and the distinction between consummated (madkhul biha) and unconsummated (ghayr madkhul biha) wives. The ruling differs based on this distinction.
The 'mahall al-talaq' (place of divorce) ends for an unconsummated wife after one talaq.
2
State the majority position and its proof
The majority (Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad) rule that two divorces occur simultaneously because 'ma'a' is for qiran (conjunction), implying both happen at once.
This is the zahir al-riwayah position.
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's objection
Abu Yusuf argues that the pronoun 'ha' is a kinayah (pronoun) that requires the antecedent (the first talaq) to be prior in existence. Thus, the first talaq occurs first, and by the time the second is pronounced, the wife is no longer a mahall for talaq.
This is a linguistic reasoning based on the nature of pronouns.
4
Apply the distinction for consummated wives
For a consummated wife, the mahall remains after one talaq (she can receive up to three). Therefore, even according to Abu Yusuf, two divorces occur because the place is still present after the first.
All scholars agree on two divorces for a consummated wife in all phrasings.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The majority view is the relied-upon position for fatwa. The commentator affirms this, and it is consistent with the principle that 'ma'a' indicates conjunction unless a clear indicator of sequence exists.
Abu Yusuf's view is a valid marjuh variant within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
انت طالق واحدة مع واحدة او معها واحده سے دو طلاقیں واقع ہوں گی ولو قال انت طالق واحدة مع واحدة او معها واحدة تقع ثنتان لان كلمة مع للقران وعن ابي يوسف في قوله معها واحدة تقع واحدة لان الكناية تقتضى سبق المكنى عنه لا محالة وفى المدخول بها تقع ثنتان في الوجوه كلها لقيام المحلية بعد وقوع الاولى ترجمہ اور اگر کہا تجھ کو ایک طالق ہے ایک کے ساتھ یا اس کے ساتھ ایک تو دو واقع ہو جائیں گی ۔ کیونکہ کلمہ مع اتصال کیلئے آتا ہے اور ابو یوسف سے روایت ہے کہ شوہر کے قول معها واحدۃ میں ایک واقع ہوگی۔ کیونکہ کنایہ مقتضی ہے کہ جس سے کنایہ کیا گیا ہے وہ سابق ہو۔ اور مدخول بہا میں تمام صورتوں میں دو واقع ہوں گی ۔ پہلی کے واقع ہونے کے بعد محل طلاق موجود ہونے کی وجہ سے۔ تشریح مسئلہ اگر کسی نے کہا انت طالق واحدة مع واحدة يا انت طالق واحدة معها واحدة تو دو طلاقیں واقع ہو جائیں گی۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ کلمہ مع اقتران و اتصال کیلئے آتا ہے نہ پس حاصل یہ ہوگا کہ دونوں ساتھ ساتھ واقع ہوئیں ۔ امام ابو یوسف کی ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ معہا واحدۃ کی صورت میں ایک واقع ہوگی۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ ضمیر سبقت مرجع کا وجودا تقاضا کرتی ہے اور طلاق میں واحدۃ جو مر جمع ہے اس کا وجود وقوع سے ہوگا ۔ تو اب صورت یہ ہوگی کہ واحدہ اولی پہلے واقع ہوئی۔ اور وقوع ثانیہ کے وقت محل طلاق ہونا فوت ہو گیا۔ لہذا شامیہ افو ہو گی۔ مصنف "فرماتے ہیں کہ مذکورہ تمام صورتوں میں مدخول بہا پر دو واقع ہوں گی ۔ کیونکہ مدخول بہا ایک کے واقع ہونے کے بعد بھی محل طلاق رہتی ہے۔
From 'you are divorced one with one' or 'with it one', two divorces occur. If he said 'you are divorced one with one' or 'with it one', two occur because the word 'with' is for conjunction. And from Abu Yusuf, in his saying 'with it one', one occurs because the pronoun necessarily requires the antecedent to be prior. And in the consummated wife, two occur in all cases due to the existence of the place after the occurrence of the first. Translation: And if he said 'you have one divorce with one or with it one', then two occur because the word 'with' comes for conjunction. And it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that in the husband's saying 'with it one', one occurs because the pronoun necessitates that which is referred to is prior. And in the consummated wife, two occur in all cases due to the existence of the place after the occurrence of the first. Explanation: If someone said 'you are divorced one with one' or 'you are divorced one with it one', two divorces occur. The proof is that the word 'with' signifies conjunction and connection. So the result is that both occur together. Imam Abu Yusuf has a narration that in the case of 'with it one', one occurs. The proof is that the pronoun requires the antecedent to exist prior, and in divorce, the 'one' which is the antecedent, its existence comes from occurrence. So now the scenario is that the first one occurred earlier, and at the time of occurrence of the second, the place of divorce is lost. Therefore, it becomes invalid. The author says that in all the mentioned cases, for the consummated wife, two occur because the consummated wife remains a place of divorce even after one has occurred.
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling when a man says to his wife 'you are divorced one with one' or 'you are divorced one with it one'. The word 'ma'a' (with) indicates conjunction (qiran), meaning both divorces occur simultaneously. Therefore, two divorces take effect at once. This is the majority Hanafi position (Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad). However, Imam Abu Yusuf has a different opinion regarding the phrase 'ma'aha wahida' (with it one). He argues that the pronoun 'ha' (it) refers back to the first divorce, implying that the first divorce must have occurred before the second. Since the first divorce occurs first (making the woman bain if unconsummated), the second divorce becomes invalid because the place (mahall) for divorce no longer exists. Thus, only one divorce occurs. The commentary then distinguishes between an unconsummated wife (ghayr madkhul biha) and a consummated wife (madkhul biha). For a consummated wife, the place for divorce remains after one divorce (she can receive up to three), so regardless of the phrasing, two divorces occur in all cases according to all scholars. The author (presumably al-Marghinani or the commentator) affirms the majority view that for the unconsummated wife, the ruling differs based on the wording, but for the consummated wife, two always occur.

Key Terms
مع (ma'a): A preposition meaning 'with'; in talaq context, it signifies conjunction (qiran) implying simultaneity.
كنایه (kināyah): A pronoun (like 'ha' in 'ma'aha') that refers back to something mentioned earlier, implying a sequence or relationship.
محل طلاق (mahall al-ṭalāq): The 'place' or capacity for talaq; for an unconsummated wife, this ends after one talaq; for a consummated wife, it remains for up to three.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man says to his unconsummated wife: 'You are divorced one with it one' (انت طالق واحدة معها واحدة). According to Imam Abu Yusuf's narration, how many divorces occur?
A) Two divorces
B) One divorce
C) No divorce
D) Three divorces

Key Takeaway
In talaq with 'with it one', the majority holds two divorces occur simultaneously, but Abu Yusuf argued only one due to the pronoun's implication of sequence; for consummated wives, all agree on two.

Talaq Phrasings for a Non-Consummated Wife
Ruling on three phrasings of multiple talaq for a non-consummated wife.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the number of divorces that occur for each of the three phrasings when pronounced upon a non-consummated wife, and explain the linguistic reasoning behind each ruling.

Core Idea
After the first talaq on a non-consummated wife, the marriage ends; any subsequent talaq is laghw unless the phrasing makes divorces simultaneous.

This passage from the Hanafi tradition teaches how the precise wording of talaq affects its legal effect. The key is understanding that a non-consummated wife becomes bain after a single talaq, so a second talaq is normally invalid. However, certain phrasings using 'before' and 'after' can cause divorces to be considered simultaneous, allowing two to fall at once. Let's examine the three phrasings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for a non-consummated wife
Recall that a non-consummated wife (غير مدخول بہا) becomes bain (irrevocably divorced) after a single talaq. Any further talaq is لغو (invalid) because the marriage no longer exists.
2
Analyze 'واحدة بعدها واحدة' (one after one)
The word 'بعد' describes what comes after. The divorce is sequential: first divorce at present, second after. Since the marriage ends with the first, the second is لغو. Only one divorce falls.
The second 'واحدة' is laghw.
3
Analyze 'واحدة قبلها واحدة' (one before one)
The word 'قبل' describes what comes after. The phrasing requires effecting the second divorce in the past and the first in the present. In Hanafi usul, effecting a talaq in the past is treated as present. Hence both fall simultaneously.
Two divorces occur together.
4
Analyze 'واحدة بعد واحد' (one after one)
Here 'بعد' describes what is before. The first divorce is in the present, the second is placed before the first (i.e., in the past). Again, past is equivalent to present, so both fall together at the present moment.
Also results in two divorces.
5
Apply the principle of simultaneity
Whenever the wording forces a second talaq to be placed in the past relative to the first, it is treated as occurring at the same present moment, allowing two divorces on a non-consummated wife.
This is only possible because a non-consummated wife can be given multiple talaq in one sitting.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واحدة بعدها واحدة اس صورت میں لفظ بعد مابعد کی صفت ہوگا۔ معنی یہ ہوں گے کہ تجھ کو ایک طلاق ہے اس کے بعد ایک ہے۔ یعنی واحد و اولی سے غیر مدخول بہا بائنہ ہوگئی۔ اس کے بعد واحدہ ثانی محل طلاق فوت ہونے کی وجہ سے لغو ہو جائے گی ۔ لہذا اس صورت میں بھی ایک ہی واقع ہوگی۔
اور اگر کہا انت طالق واحدة قبلها واحدة اس صورت میں لفظ قبل ما بعد کی صفت ہوگا یعنی تجھ کو ایک طلاق ہے اس سے پہلے ایک ۔ یہ کلام تقاضا کرتا ہے ایقاع ثانیہ کا ماضی میں اور ایقاع اولی کا حال میں اور چونکہ ایقاع فی الماضی ایقاع فی الحال ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا دونوں طلاقیں زمانہ حال میں ساتھ ساتھ واقع ہوں گی اور غیر مدخول بہا بیوی کو یکبارگی دو طلاقیں دی جاسکتی ہیں۔ اسلئے اس صورت میں دو واقع ہوں گی ۔ اور اگر کہا انت طالق واحدة بعد واحد و یعنی تجھ کو ایک طلاق ہے بعد ایک کے اس صورت میں لفظ بعد ماقبل کی صفت ہوگا۔ اور یہ کلام تقاضا کرے گا اولی کو واقع کرنے کا زمانہ حال میں اور ثانیہ کو اولی سے پہلے اور ظاہر ہے کہ اولی کے وقوع سے پہلے کا زمانہ ماضی ہوگا تو گویا کہ ثانیہ کو زمانہ ماضی میں واقع کیا گیا ہے۔ اور چونکہ ایقاع فی الماضی ایقاع فی الحال ہوتا ہے لہذا یہ دونوں طلاقیں زمانہ حال میں ساتھ ساتھ واقع ہوں گی۔ اس وجہ سے اس صورت میں بھی غیر مدخول بہا پر دو واقع ہو جائیں گی۔
For 'one after one', in this case the word 'after' is an adjective of what is after. The meaning is: you have one divorce, after that one. That is, from 'one' and 'first', the non-consummated wife becomes bain. After that, the second 'one' becomes لغو (irrelevant) because the place of divorce is lost. Therefore in this case also only one falls. And if he said 'you are divorced one before one', in this case the word 'before' is an adjective of what is after, meaning you have one divorce, before it one. This speech requires effecting the second in the past and the first in the present, and since effecting in the past is like effecting in the present, therefore both divorces occur together in the present, and a non-consummated wife can be given two divorces at once. Hence in this case two fall. And if he said 'you are divorced one after one', in this case the word 'after' is an adjective of what is before, and this speech requires effecting the first in the present and the second before the first, and it is apparent that the time before the occurrence of the first is the past, so it is as if the second was effected in the past, and since effecting in the past is like effecting in the present, therefore both divorces occur together in the present. For this reason in this case also two fall on the non-consummated wife.
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage discusses the effect of different phrasings of talaq using words like 'after' and 'before' when a husband says multiple divorces. For a non-consummated wife (غير مدخول بہا), only one talaq takes effect immediately, making her bain (irrevocably divorced). Any subsequent talaq becomes لغو (invalid) because the marriage has already ended. However, if the wording indicates simultaneous effect, two divorces can fall. The author explains three cases: (1) 'واحدة بعدها واحدة' (one after one): only one falls because the second is after the first, but by then the marriage is over. (2) 'واحدة قبلها واحدة' (one before one): both fall at the present moment because the second is placed in the past, which is equivalent to the present in effect. (3) 'واحدة بعد واحد' (one after one): similar to the second, both fall simultaneously because the second is placed before the first. The key is linguistic analysis: the words 'before' and 'after' determine whether the divorces are sequential or simultaneous, affecting whether more than one can occur on a non-consummated wife.

Key Terms
غیر مدخول بہا (ghayr madkhul biha): A wife who has not been consummated; her marriage ends with a single talaq (ba'in).
لغو (laghw): Invalid or irrelevant; a talaq that has no effect because the marriage has already ended.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Two
C) Three
D) None

Key Takeaway
When pronouncing talaq on a non-consummated wife, only one talaq takes effect; any additional talaq is laghw unless the wording forces simultaneity.

Ruling for 'واحدة مع واحدة' or 'معها واحدة' in Talaq: Majority and Abu Yusuf's View
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the effect of 'مع' and pronoun 'ها' in talaq phrasing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi majority and Abu Yusuf's positions on the number of divorces falling when phrasing includes 'مع', and explain the linguistic reasoning behind each.

Core Idea
The word 'مع' indicates conjunction (two divorces fall), but the pronoun 'ها' in 'معها' may imply sequence (only one falls according to Abu Yusuf).

The precise wording used in divorce can change the legal outcome. This passage examines two similar phrasings—'واحدة مع واحدة' and 'معها واحدة'—and reveals an intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether one or two divorces fall on a non-consummated wife. Understanding the linguistic reasoning will sharpen your ability to apply talaq rulings correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two phrasings and their common element
Both phrasings use the word 'مع' (with). The first is 'واحدة مع واحدة' (one with one), the second is 'معها واحدة' (with it one). The pronoun 'ها' in 'معها' refers back to the first divorce.
The difference is whether the second divorce is mentioned independently or linked via a pronoun.
2
State the majority ruling for both phrasings
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, for a non-consummated wife, two divorces fall in both phrasings because the word 'مع' indicates conjunction (qiran) and simultaneity.
The majority view treats both phrasings as identical in effect.
3
Identify Abu Yusuf's ikhtilaf for 'معها واحدة'
Abu Yusuf holds that when the husband says 'معها واحدة', only one divorce falls on a non-consummated wife. He argues that the pronoun 'ها' requires the first divorce to precede, so the second is subsequent and ineffective after the marriage ends.
This ruling applies only to the non-consummated case; for a consummated wife, all agree two fall.
4
Analyze the linguistic reasoning
The majority focuses on the word 'مع' itself, which normally means conjunction. Abu Yusuf focuses on the pronoun 'ها', which grammatically requires an antecedent that already exists, implying sequence rather than simultaneity.
Both sides rely on valid linguistic principles, leading to legitimate ikhtilaf.
5
Note the exception for the consummated wife
In the case of a consummated wife (madkhul biha), there is no dispute: two divorces fall in both phrasings because after the first divorce, the wife remains in marriage until the 'iddah expires, providing a continuing basis for the second divorce.
The thamarah al-khilaf only appears in the non-consummated scenario.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قال انت طالق واحدة مع واحدة او معها واحدة تقع ثنتان لان كلمة مع للقران وعن ابي يوسف في قوله معها واحدة تقع واحدة لان الكناية تقتضى سبق المكنى عنه لا محالة وفى المدخول بها تقع ثنتان في الوجوه كلها لقيام المحلية بعد وقوع الاولى
ترجمہ اور اگر کہا تجھ کو ایک طالق ہے ایک کے ساتھ یا اس کے ساتھ ایک تو دو واقع ہو جائیں گی ۔ کیونکہ کلمہ مع اتصال کیلئے آتا ہے اور ابو یوسف سے روایت ہے کہ شوہر کے قول معها واحدۃ میں ایک واقع ہوگی۔ کیونکہ کنایہ مقتضی ہے کہ جس سے کنایہ کیا گیا ہے وہ سابق ہو۔ اور مدخول بہا میں تمام صورتوں میں دو واقع ہوں گی ۔ پہلی کے واقع ہونے کے بعد محل طلاق موجود ہونے کی وجہ سے۔
And if he said 'you are divorced one with one' or 'with it one', two fall because the word 'مع' is for conjunction. And from Abu Yusuf, in his saying 'معها واحدة' one falls because the pronoun (kinaayah) requires that what is referred to precedes necessarily. And in the consummated (wife), two fall in all cases because the place of divorce remains after the first falls. Translation: And if he said 'you are divorced one with one' or 'with it one', two fall, because the word 'مع' is for connection. And from Abu Yusuf it is narrated that in the husband's saying 'معها واحدة', one will fall, because the pronoun requires that which is referred to precede. And in the consummated wife, two fall in all cases due to the existence of the place of divorce after the first occurs.
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage addresses two phrasings: 'واحدة مع واحدة' (one with one) and 'معها واحدة' (with it one). The majority view (Imam Muhammad and Abu Hanifa according to the text) is that two divorces fall on a non-consummated wife because 'مع' indicates conjunction and simultaneity. However, Abu Yusuf has a different view for 'معها واحدة': he argues that the pronoun 'ها' (it) in 'معها' necessarily refers to something already mentioned, meaning the first divorce must have occurred first, so the second is after the first and thus ineffective on a non-consummated wife. For a consummated wife (مدخول بہا), all agree that two divorces fall in both phrasings because after the first divorce, the wife remains in the marriage (the place of divorce still exists) until the 'iddah ends.

Key Terms
مع (ma'a): The preposition meaning 'with', indicating conjunction and simultaneity.
کنایہ (kinaayah): A pronoun reference; here specifically the suffix 'ها' in 'معها' which refers back to the first talaq.

Conditional Talaq with 'واو' and 'فاء': The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on conditional talaq with waw and fa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Hanifa's and the Sahibayn's positions on the number of divorces that fall when a condition precedes two divorces joined by 'واو', and apply the same reasoning to the 'فاء' case, identifying the preferred view.

Core Idea
When 'واو' joins two divorces after a condition, doubt over sequence reduces the count to one.

This passage examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute regarding conditional talaq with a non-consummated wife. The key question: if a husband says 'If you enter the house, you are divorced one and one', how many divorces fall upon entry? Abu Hanifa says one, the Sahibayn say two. The difference hinges on the linguistic interpretation of the conjunction 'واو' (and) and the role of doubt. We also explore how using 'فاء' (then) changes the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The husband says to a non-consummated wife: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced one and one.' Note that the condition precedes the pronouncement of talaq. The two divorces are joined by 'واو'.
Non-consummated wife is significant because a third divorce is not needed to make it irrevocable; the number matters for finality.
2
State Abu Hanifa's ruling and proof
Abu Hanifa holds that only one divorce falls. His proof: 'واو' can mean either conjunction (simultaneity) or sequence (tarub). Because of this ambiguity (shakk), we apply the lesser number, just as in immediate pronouncement (without condition) where only one falls by default due to doubt.
The principle: doubt in the number of divorces leads to the lesser count.
3
State the Sahibayn's ruling and proof
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) hold that two divorces fall. Their proof: 'واو' is for absolute conjunction (al-jam' al-mutlaq), so both divorces are attached to the condition as a single unit, just as if he said 'two' explicitly or delayed the condition.
They argue there is no ambiguity here; the conjunction is clear.
4
Contrast with the condition-later scenario
If the husband says 'You are divorced one and one if you enter the house' (condition later), there is consensus (ijma') that two divorces fall. Because the condition comes after, it modifies the entire statement, making both divorces dependent on entry simultaneously.
This shows that word order matters in determining the effect of the condition.
5
Apply to the 'فاء' case
If 'فاء' is used instead of 'واو' (e.g., 'If you enter, you are divorced one then one'), there is disagreement. Al-Karkhi said the same dispute applies, but Faqih Abu al-Layth claimed consensus that only one divorce falls because 'فاء' denotes immediate succession (ta'qib), meaning the second divorce would occur after the first has already ended the marriage. Al-Hidayah prefers Abu al-Layth's view as more correct.
The difference between 'واو' (ambiguous) and 'فاء' (clear sequence) affects the outcome.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولوقال لها ان دخلت الدارفانت طالق واحدة وواحدة فدخلت وقعت عليها واحدة عندابي حنيفة وقالا تقع ثنتان ولوقال لها انت طالق واحدة وواحدة ان دخلت الدار فدخلت طلقت ثنتين بالاجماع لهما ان حرف الواو للجمع المطلق فتعلقن جملة كما اذانص على الثنتين او اخر الشرط وله ان الجمع المطلق يحتمل القران والترتيب فعلى اعتبار الاول تقع ثنتان وعلى اعتبار الثانى لاتقع الا واحدة كما اذا انجز بهذه اللفظة فلايقع الزائد على الواحدة بالشك بخلاف ما اذا اخر الشرط لانه مغير صدر الكلام فيتوقف الاول عليه فيقعن جملة ولا مغير فيما اذاقدم الشرط فلم يتوقف ولو عطف بحرف الفاء فهو على هذا الخلاف فيما ذكر الكرخى وذكر الفقيه ابو اللي انه يقع واحدة بالاتفاق لان الفاء للتعقيب وهو الاصح ترجمہ اور اگر غیر مدخول بہا سے کہا اگر تو مکان میں داخل ہوئی تو تجھ کو ایک طلاق ہے اور ایک ۔ پھر داخل ہوگئی تو اس پر امام صاحب کے نزدیک ایک واقع ہوگی۔ اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ دو واقع ہو جائیں گی۔ اور اگر کہا اس سے تجھ کو ایک طلاق ہے اور اگر تو داخل ہوئی مکان میں ۔ پھر داخل ہوگئی تو بالا جماع دو واقع ہوں گی۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے حرف داد مطلق جمع کیلئے ہے۔ پس ( دونوں طلاقیں ) جمع ہو کر معلق ہوں گی جیسا کہ جب دو کی صراحت کی ہو یا شرط کو مؤخر کیا ہو۔ اور امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جمع مطلق قرآن اور ترتیب کا احتمال رکھتی ہے۔ پس اول کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے دو واقع ہوں گی اور ثانی کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے صرف ایک واقع ہوگی ۔ جیسا کہ جب اس لفظ کے ساتھ فی الحال دے دے تو شک کی وجہ سے ایک سے زائد واقع نہیں ہو گی ۔ بخلاف اس صورت کے جبکہ شرط کومو خر کیا ہو ۔ کیونکہ شرط اول کلام کو بدل دینے والی ہے۔ پس اول کلام شرط پر موقوف رہے گا ۔ لہذا اسب یکبارگی واقع ہوں گی ۔ اور اس صورت میں کوئی مغیر نہیں جبکہ شرط کو مقدم کیا ہو۔ پس موقوف نہیں رہا۔ اور اگر حرف فاء کے ساتھ عطف کیا تو وہ اسی اختلاف پر ہے امام کرخی کے ذکر کے مطابق ۔ اور فقیہ ابواللیث نے ذکر کیا کہ بالا تفاق ایک واقع ہوگی۔ کیونکہ فاء تعقیب کیلئے ہے اور یہی اصح ہے۔
And if he said to her 'if you enter the house, then you are divorced one and one', and she entered, one falls according to Abu Hanifa, and the two (Sahibayn) said two fall. And if he said to her 'you are divorced one and one if you enter the house', and she entered, she is divorced by two by consensus. Their (Sahibayn's) proof is that the letter 'واو' is for absolute conjunction, so they are attached as a single sentence, just as if he explicitly stated two or delayed the condition. And his (Abu Hanifa's) proof is that absolute conjunction can mean both conjunction and sequence; if the first is considered, two fall, and if the second is considered, only one falls, just as when he executes (immediate pronouncement) with this word, then more than one does not fall due to doubt. Unlike when he delays the condition, because it changes the start of the speech, so the first depends on it, so they fall together. And there is no change when he precedes the condition, so it does not depend. And if he uses the letter 'فاء' for conjunction, then it is on this dispute according to what Karkhi mentioned, and Faqih Abu al-Layth mentioned that by agreement one falls, because 'فاء' is for immediate succession, and this is more correct. Translation: And if he said to a non-consummated wife 'if you enter the house, then you are divorced one and one', then she entered, then according to Imam (Abu Hanifa) one will fall, and the two (Sahibayn) said two fall. And if he said to her 'you are divorced one and one if you enter the house', then she entered, then by consensus two fall. Sahibayn's proof is that the letter 'واو' is for absolute conjunction, so both are attached together as conditional, just as if he explicitly stated two or delayed the condition. And Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that absolute conjunction can mean both conjunction and sequence; if the first is considered, two fall, and if the second is considered, only one falls, just as when he gives immediately with this word, then more than one does not fall due to doubt. Unlike the case when he delays the condition, because the condition changes the beginning of the speech, so the first depends on it, so they fall together. And there is no changer when the condition is advanced, so it does not depend. And if he uses the letter 'فاء' for conjunction, then it is on this dispute according to what Karkhi mentioned, and Faqih Abu al-Layth mentioned that by agreement one falls, because 'فاء' is for immediate succession, and this is more correct.
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This passage details an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding conditional talaq when two divorces are mentioned with the conjunction 'واو' (and). The focus is on non-consummated wives. There are two scenarios: (1) condition precedes: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced one and one'. (2) condition follows: 'You are divorced one and one if you enter the house'. In the second scenario, there is consensus (ijma') that two divorces fall because the condition affects both parts equally. In the first scenario, Abu Hanifa rules that only one divorce falls, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) rule that two fall. The difference is based on the interpretation of the الواو (waw). Sahibayn argue that الواو means absolute conjunction, so both divorces are attached to the condition as a single unit, just as if the husband said 'two' explicitly. Abu Hanifa argues that الواو can also imply sequence (tarub), and when there is ambiguity (doubt), the safer course is to apply only one divorce (since more than one on a non-consummated wife is irrevocable and should not be based on doubt). He draws an analogy to immediate pronouncement (without condition) where only one falls due to doubt. When using 'فاء' (then) instead of 'واو', there is disagreement: Karkhi said the same ikhtilaf applies, but Abu al-Layth claimed consensus that only one divorce falls because 'فاء' indicates succession (ta'qib), implying the second after the first, and the first ends the marriage. Al-Hidayah favors Abu al-Layth's view as more correct.

Key Terms
جمع مطلق (al-jam' al-mutlaq): Absolute conjunction; the meaning of 'wa' as joining two things without specifying order.
تعقیب (ta'qib): Immediate succession; the meaning of 'فاء' as indicating that the second follows the first.
شک (shakk): Doubt; a state of uncertainty that legally prevents establishing a certain ruling, especially in matters of talaq.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One divorce falls, by consensus.
B) Two divorces fall, by consensus.
C) Dispute between Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn.
D) No divorce falls because the condition is not fulfilled.

Key Takeaway
When a condition precedes two divorces joined by 'واو', there is an intra-Hanafi dispute; Abu Hanifa holds one falls, Sahibayn say two; for 'فاء', the preferred view is one.

Multiple Conditional Talaq with 'Wa' – Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on multiple conditional talaq with 'wa'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on multiple conditional talaq with 'wa' and explain why Abu Hanifa rules one divorce while the Sahibayn rule two.

Core Idea
The conjunction 'wa' creates doubt between simultaneity and sequence, so only one talaq occurs when the condition precedes.

This lesson examines a well-known intra-Hanafi dispute regarding conditional talaq when a husband says to his non-consummated wife, 'If you enter the house, you are divorced one and one' (wa used). The disagreement hinges on the legal interpretation of the Arabic conjunction 'wa' (and). Abu Hanifa holds that 'wa' can imply either simultaneity or sequence; since both are possible, doubt prevents the occurrence of more than one talaq. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that 'wa' indicates absolute conjunction, so both divorces occur together upon fulfillment of the condition. We will walk through the proofs, the rebuttal, and the practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and the two positions
Identify the exact wording of the conditional talaq: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced one and one.' Then note that Abu Hanifa rules one divorce and the Sahibayn rule two.
The wife is ghayr madkhul biha (non-consummated), which affects the outcome after the first talaq.
2
Analyze the linguistic meaning of 'wa'
Determine whether 'wa' in Arabic indicates absolute conjunction (jam' mutlaq) as the Sahibayn claim, or whether it can also imply sequence (tartib) as Abu Hanifa claims. This is the root of the dispute.
The analysis is based on usul al-fiqh: the word 'wa' is considered ambiguous (mushtarak) in Hanafi usul.
3
Examine the Sahibayn's analogy
The Sahibayn analogize to the case where the condition is postponed (e.g., 'You are divorced one and one if you enter'), where by consensus two divorces occur. They argue that the same should apply when the condition is advanced.
The analogy is based on the idea that 'wa' joins the two divorces absolutely, regardless of word order.
4
Evaluate Abu Hanifa's rebuttal
Abu Hanifa distinguishes between condition postponed and condition advanced. In postponement, the condition changes the opening part of the sentence, so both divorces depend on the condition and occur together. In advancement, there is no change, so the divorces are interpreted sequentially. Additionally, immediate (munajjaz) talaq 'one and one' results in only one divorce due to doubt.
The key point: doubt (shakk) prevents the occurrence of additional talaq.
5
Note the ruling for 'fa' and the tarjih
If the conjunction is 'fa' (then), Abu al-Layth's view that only one divorce occurs by consensus is considered more correct (asahh). This provides guidance for fatwa.
The text does not explicitly prefer one view for 'wa', but the reasoning of Abu Hanifa is often adopted in later Hanafi practice.

And if he said to her, 'If you enter the house, then you are divorced one and one,' and she entered, then according to Abu Hanifa one divorce occurs, and they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said two occur. And if he said, 'You are divorced one and one if you enter the house,' and she entered, then by consensus two occur. Their proof is that the letter waw is for absolute conjunction, so they are attached together as a whole, as if he explicitly said two or if the condition is postponed. His proof is that absolute conjunction can imply simultaneity or sequence. If the first is considered, two occur; if the second, only one occurs, as when he gives with this word immediately, then no more than one occur due to doubt, unlike when the condition is postponed because it changes the beginning of the speech, so the first depends on it and they occur together, and there is no changer when the condition is advanced, so it does not depend. If he connects with the letter fa, then the same disagreement exists as mentioned by al-Karkhi, and al-Faqih Abu al-Layth mentioned that by agreement one occurs because fa is for succession, and that is more correct. Translation: And if he said to a non-consummated wife, 'If you enter the house, then you are divorced one and one,' then she entered, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa one occurs, and the Sahibayn said two occur. And if he said, 'You are divorced one and one if you enter the house,' then she entered, then by consensus two occur. The Sahibayn's proof: The letter waw is for absolute conjunction, so both divorces are attached together as suspended, like when he explicitly says two or when the condition is postponed. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof: Absolute conjunction can imply simultaneity or sequence. By the first, two occur; by the second, only one occurs, as when he immediately gives with this word, then no more than one occurs due to doubt, unlike when the condition is postponed because the condition changes the beginning of the speech, so the first depends on it, thus they occur at once, and there is no changer when the condition is advanced, so it does not depend. If he connects with the letter fa, then there is disagreement according to al-Karkhi, and al-Faqih Abu al-Layth said that by agreement one occurs because fa is for succession, and that is more correct. Explanation: The scenario is that if multiple divorces are suspended on a condition and one is connected to the other by waw, there are two cases: condition advanced or postponed. If postponed, e.g., 'You are divorced one and one if you enter the house,' then she enters, by consensus both occur. If condition is advanced, e.g., 'If you enter the house, then you are divorced one and one,' and a non-consummated wife enters, then according to Sahibayn two occur, and according to Imam one occurs. The Sahibayn's proof: The word waw absolutely indicates conjunction, so both divorces are attached together and occur at once, as in the case of saying 'If you enter the house, then you are divorced two' because conjunction with waw is like using the word 'two'. And just as when condition is postponed both occur by consensus, so also when advanced both occur. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof: Absolute conjunction can imply simultaneity or sequence. If simultaneity is intended, two occur; if sequence, one occurs, as in immediate divorce 'You are divorced one and one' where only one occurs. It is known that there is doubt about more than one, and divorce does not occur with doubt, so more than one does not occur. The Sahibayn analogized the case of advanced condition to postponed condition; we say this analogy is not correct because in postponement the condition changes the first part of speech, so the first depends on the condition, thus after condition occurs both divorces happen at once. In advancement, there is nothing to change the first part, so the first does not depend on the last, hence both divorces occur sequentially, and since the wife is non-consummated, she becomes bain by the first one, and the second does not occur. Similarly, analogy to saying 'You are divorced two' is not correct because specifying two removes any possibility of sequence, whereas waw retains the possibility of sequence, so analogy with difference is invalid. And if he connects with fa, e.g., 'You are divorced one then one,' then according to al-Karkhi it is also disputed: according to Imam one, according to Sahibayn two. Al-Karkhi equated conjunction with waw and fa, but this is incorrect. And al-Faqih Abu al-Layth says that with fa, by agreement one divorce occurs and this is more correct because fa indicates succession, i.e., sequential order of rulings.
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the effect of the conjunction 'wa' (and) when multiple divorces are suspended on a condition. The matn (original text) states the different positions and their proofs. The commentary (sharh) expands on the reasoning and addresses the analogy proposed by the Sahibayn. The core issue is whether 'wa' implies simultaneous occurrence or allows for sequential occurrence. Abu Hanifa argues that since 'wa' can mean either, and since in immediate (munajjaz) divorce only one occurs when 'wa' is used, the same doubt applies here, so only one divorce occurs. The Sahibayn argue that 'wa' is for absolute conjunction, so both divorces are linked and occur together when the condition is fulfilled. The commentary then refutes the Sahibayn's analogy by distinguishing between condition postponed (where the condition changes the ruling) and condition advanced (where it does not). The final part discusses 'fa' (then), where the relied-upon view (from al-Faqih Abu al-Layth) is that only one divorce occurs by consensus. This passage demonstrates the Hanafi method of linguistic analysis, analogical reasoning (qiyas), and rebuttal of opposing views.

Key Terms
واو (waw): The Arabic conjunction 'and', which can imply either simultaneity (جمع القران) or sequence (جمع الترتيب) according to Abu Hanifa, while the Sahibayn consider it for absolute conjunction without sequence.
فاء (fa): The Arabic conjunction 'then', indicating immediate succession (تعقيب). Here, it is used in conditional talaq to show sequential occurrence.
غير مدخول بها (ghayr madkhul biha): A wife with whom the husband has not consummated the marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the Sahibayn, how many divorces occur if a husband says to his non-consummated wife, 'If you enter the house, you are divorced one and one' (wa used), and she enters?
A) One divorce
B) Two divorces
C) Three divorces
D) No divorce

Key Takeaway
In conditional talaq with 'wa', Abu Hanifa rules one divorce due to ambiguity and doubt; the Sahibayn rule two; the later preferred view is Abu Hanifa's.
